Qada for Insanity or Unconsciousness: The Five-Prayer Limit
Ruling statement on qada for insanity/unconsciousness with a limit of five prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for missed prayers due to insanity or unconsciousness and apply the five-prayer threshold to determine whether qada is obligatory.

Core Idea
Insanity or unconsciousness beyond five prayers lifts the obligation to make them up entirely.

This lesson addresses a distinctive Hanafi ruling that provides relief for prolonged loss of legal responsibility. While most schools require qada for every missed prayer regardless of duration, the Hanafi school sets a limit: if insanity or unconsciousness lasts up to five prayer times, those prayers must be made up; if it exceeds five, the obligation drops. This ruling balances accountability with mercy, recognizing that an extended period of incapacity would cause undue hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse
The ruling applies specifically to insanity (junun) and unconsciousness (ighma'). These remove legal responsibility (taklif). Note that other excuses like sleep or forgetfulness have different rules.
2
Measure the duration
Count the number of consecutive prayer times missed. According to the Hanafi school, a complete day includes five prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha).
The count is based on prayer times, not days.
3
Apply the threshold
If the duration is up to five prayer times, qada is wajib for all missed prayers. If it exceeds five, no qada is required for any of them — including the first five.
The entire obligation falls away once the condition persists beyond the limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جن او اغمى عليه إلى خمس صلوات يقضيها، وازيد من خمس لا يقضيها (۲۹۷) ترجمه : (۲۹۷) اور جو پانچوں نمازوں تک مجنون یا بیہوش رہے تو قضا کرے، اور پانچ سے زیادہ ہوتو قضا نہ کرے۔
And whoever is insane or unconscious up to five prayers, he makes them up; if more than five, he does not make them up. Translation: (297) And whoever remains insane or unconscious for up to five prayers, he should make them up; if more than five, he does not make them up.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage states a ruling (hukm) regarding the obligation of qada (making up) for missed prayers due to insanity (junun) or unconsciousness (ighma'). The Hanafi school distinguishes between two durations: if the condition lasts for up to five prayer times, the person must make up those prayers after recovery. However, if the condition persists for more than five prayers, the obligation to make up the missed prayers is dropped entirely (saqit). The limit of five prayers is based on ease and the principle that excessive duration imposes hardship. This ruling is specific to insanity and unconsciousness; for other excuses like sleep, all prayers must be made up. The school relies on reports from the Companions (athar) and the principle of maslahah (public benefit).

Key Terms
جنون (junūn): Insanity or mental derangement that removes legal responsibility.
إغماء (ighmā'): Unconsciousness, fainting.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed obligatory act after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must make up all six prayers.
B) He must make up the first five prayers only.
C) He does not need to make any of the prayers.
D) He must make up the prayers of the first day only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides relief by not requiring qada for prolonged insanity or unconsciousness beyond five prayers.

Prayer of the Sick: According to Ability and Building Upon It
Ruling on sick prayer and building upon recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sick person's prayer and explain the condition for building upon a prayer when health returns.

Core Idea
The sick pray to ability; building is allowed from sitting, not from lying.

Illness does not remove the obligation of prayer; rather, the form adapts to the person's capacity. This lesson covers the general rule for the sick and a specific scenario where health returns mid-prayer, focusing on the Hanafi position and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is the obligatory prayer (salat) for a sick person. The general ruling from the text: the sick completes the prayer to the extent possible, even with gestures (ima).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites Quran 48:17 and the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn to support the principle of praying according to ability. Note the Hanafi use of these texts.
3
Examine the building rule
The second part: if a person prays sitting with ruku and sujud and becomes healthy, he may build upon that prayer. The principle is that sitting is similar (qarib) to standing.
4
Identify the exception
If the person prayed lying down with gestures, he cannot build upon that because lying is not similar to standing. The prayer must be restarted.
5
Understand the usul principle
The underlying principle is that building (bina) is allowed transformation between similar postures. This is derived from the Prophet's practice in voluntary prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المريض

مرض يتمها بما قدر ولو بالايماء في المشهور (۲۹۶) ولو صلى قاعدا يركع و يسجد فصح بنى

تشریح : تندرسی کی حالت میں رکوع سجدے کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اور درمیان میں بیماری پیش آگئی تو اب جس طرح اشارہ وغیرہ سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہو پڑھے نماز ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (1) اس آیت میں ہے۔ لیـس عـلـى الاعـمـي حرج ولا على الاعرج حرج ولا على المريض حرج . ( آیت ۱۷ سورة الفتح ۴۸) (۲) عن عمران بن حصين قال كانت بی بواسیر فسألت رسول الله الله الصلوة فقال صل قائما فان لم تستطع فقاعدا فان لم تستطع فعلى جنب ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب اذالم يطق قاعدا صلی علی جب ص ۱۷۹، نمبر ۷ ۱۱ ارترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء ان صلوة القاعد على النصف من صلوۃ القائم، ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۳۷۲ را ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی صلوۃ القاعد ، ص ۱۴۵، نمبر ۹۵۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کھڑا نہ ہو سکتا ہو تو بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھے ، اور وہ بھی نہ کر سکتا ہو تو اشارہ سے نماز پڑھے۔

ترجمه : (۲۹۶) اور اگر بیٹھ کر رکوع و سجود سے نماز پڑھتا ہو پھر نماز ہی میں تندرست ہو جائے تو اس پر بنا کر لیوے۔ ہاں اگر اشارہ سے پڑھتا ہوتو بنانہ کرے۔

تشريح : بیٹھنا کھڑے ہونے کے قریب ہے اس لئے اگر بیٹھ کر رکوع اور سجدہ کر رہا تھا اور درمیان میں تندرست ہو گیا اور کھڑے ہونے پر قدرت ہو گئی تو اس پر بنا کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر لیٹ کر اشارے سے نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اور کھڑا ہونے پر قدرت ہو گئی تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے، پہلی نماز پر بنا نہیں کرسکتا، کیونکہ لیٹنا کھڑا ہونے کے قریب نہیں ہے۔

وجه : (۱) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے . عن عائشة ان رسول الله كان يصلي جالسا فيقرأ وهو جالس فاذا بقى من قرأته قدر ما يـكـون ثلثين او اربـعـيـن آية قام فقرأ وهو قائم ثم ركع ثم سجد ثم يفعل في الثانية مثل ذلك. (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما وقاعدا ص ۲۹۷، نمبر ۱۷۰۴/۷۳۱) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھی ہے پھر آخر میں کھڑے ہو کر اس پر بنا کیا ہے۔ یہ حدیث اگر چہ نوافل کے بارے میں ہے لیکن اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بیماری کی صورت میں فرائض میں بھی بیٹھنے پر کھڑا ہونے کو بنا کر سکتا ہے۔

اصول : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ بیٹھنا کھڑا ہونے کے قریب ہے۔ اسلئے ایک دوسرے پر بناء کر سکتا ہے۔ اور لیٹنا کھڑے ہونے کے قریب نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک دوسرے پر بنا نہیں کر سکتا۔
Chapter: Prayer of the sick. The sick completes it as much as he is able, even by gesture, according to the well-known view. And if he prays sitting and performs ruku and sujud, then he becomes healthy, he builds upon it. Explanation: ... [detailed Urdu commentary with proofs]

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: (1) The sick person prays according to his ability, even by gesture, based on Quran 48:17 and the hadith of Imran bin Husayn. (2) If a person praying sitting with ruku and sujud becomes healthy during the prayer, he may build upon it and stand, because sitting is similar to standing. But if he was praying lying down with gestures, he cannot build upon it because lying is not similar to standing. The principle is that one can build from near to far, but not from far to near.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): The obligatory ritual prayer performed by Muslims five times daily.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesture, especially by head or eyes, used when unable to perform physical bowing and prostration.
بناء (bina'): Building upon a previous prayer when changing posture from sitting to standing due to health recovery.

C) He must continue sitting and cannot change posture.
D) He may gesture if unable to stand.

Key Takeaway
The sick pray according to ability; building upon a prayer is allowed only when the new posture is similar (sitting to standing) but not from lying to standing.

Insanity or Unconsciousness for Five Prayers or More
Ruling with proof on qada for missed prayers due to prolonged loss of legal responsibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed prayers when a person is insane or unconscious for five or more prayers, and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
If insanity or unconsciousness lasts more than one day and night (five prayers), qada is not required.

This lesson addresses a practical relief in the Hanafi school: when a person loses consciousness or becomes insane for an extended period, they are not burdened with making up every single missed prayer. The rule balances the obligation of prayer with the principle of removing hardship. We will explore the exact limit and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Read the matn: 'Whoever becomes insane or unconscious for five prayers must make them up, but if more, he does not.' Identify the key limit.
The limit is five prayers, which corresponds to one day and night.
2
Identify the evidence
Locate the hadith from Aisha and the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Understand how these support the ruling.
The hadith indicates no qada for prolonged unconsciousness beyond the time of a single prayer.
3
Understand the rationale
The principle is to remove hardship (raf' al-haraj). Making up many prayers after recovery would be overly burdensome.
This is consistent with the Hanafi use of istihsan based on necessity.
4
Note the limit
The limit is exactly five prayers (one day and night). If the condition lasts shorter, qada is wajib. If longer, no qada.
Some narrations mention 'one day and night' as the threshold.
5
Compare with other views
Some later scholars and other madhhabs may require qada for all missed prayers regardless of duration. Understand the difference.
The Hanafi view is considered a concession (rukhsah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جُنّ او اغمى عليه خمس صلوات قضى ولو اكثر لا

تشریح : ایک دن رات سے زیادہ بیہوش رہا ہو، یا مجنون رہا ہو اس کو قضا نہ کرے، اور اس سے کم رہا ہو تو اس کی نماز قضا کرے

وجه : (ا) عن القاسم أنه سأل عائشة عن الرجل يغمى عليه فيترك الصلوة اليوم و اليومين وأكثر من ذالک ، فقالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ليس بشيء من ذالك قضاء الا أن يغمى عليه في صلاته فيفيق و هو في وقتها فيصليها - (سنن بھتی، باب اسمی علیہ یفیق بعد ذهاب الوقتين فلا یکون علیه قضوهما، ج اول ص ۵۷۱ نمبر ۱۸۲۰) (۲) ایک دن سے زیادہ نماز قضا ہوئی ہو اور اس کو ادا کروائیں تو مریض کو تکلیف ہوگی اس لئے (۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال : كان يقول في المغمى عليه : اذا أغمى عليه يوم و ليلة أعاد و اذا كان اكثر من ذالك لم يعد ۔ ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما یعید انمی علیه من الصلوة ، ج ثانی ہیں اے نمبر ۶۵۹ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب صلوة المريض على الدابة وصلوة المغمی علیہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۷ نمبر ۴۱۶۵ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ایک دن رات کے اندر ہو تو اسکو قضاء کمرے اور اس سے زیادہ ہو تو قضاء نہ کرے۔
And whoever becomes insane or unconscious for (the time of) five prayers makes them up, but if more, he does not. Explanation: If unconscious for more than one day and night, he does not make up; if less, he does. Evidence: Hadith from Aisha and athar from Ibrahim.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This rule states that a person who becomes insane or unconscious for the duration of up to five prayers must make them up when they recover. However, if the condition lasts longer than that (more than one day and night, i.e., exceeding the time of five prayers), they are excused from making them up. The proof is from the practice of the Companions and the principle of avoiding hardship. The evidence includes a hadith from Aisha and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Insanity or mental derangement that prevents one from being legally responsible.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness, fainting, or coma.
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed obligatory prayers after their prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is unconscious for three days and nights (approximately 15 prayers), what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must make up all 15 prayers.
B) He must make up only the first five prayers.
C) He does not need to make up any prayers.
D) He must make up the prayers for the third day only.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qada of missed prayers due to insanity or unconsciousness is only required up to the duration of five prayers (one day and night); beyond that, no qada is required.

intermediate
8 min
No Obligation of Will for Missed Prayers/Fasts When Unable to Perform
Ruling with proof on dropping of obligation due to persisting excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making a will for missed prayers/fasts when the excuse persists until death, and apply the principle of isqat to similar cases.

Core Idea
What is excused by a valid shari'ah concession does not become a debt after death.

In this lesson, we examine a critical Hanafi principle: when a person misses prayers or fasts due to a valid excuse (like illness or travel) and dies before the excuse ends, there is no requirement to make a will for fidyah. The obligation was suspended and never revived, so it drops entirely. We will explore the reasoning and its application to three specific scenarios involving a sick person unable to pray, a traveler who breaks a fast before settling, and a sick person who breaks a fast before recovery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary scenario and ruling
The text begins with a sick person who cannot pray even by gesture. The ruling: he is not required to make a will for missed prayers (fidyah). Note that the ruling applies even if the number of missed prayers is small.
The key is the inability to perform even the minimal form of prayer (by gesture).
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on the principle of rukhsah (concession). The shari'ah excused the person due to genuine inability. Since health was not regained, the obligation was never firmly established. Thus, it is not considered a debt to be compensated after death.
This is qiyas khafi (latent analogy) on the idea that an excuse removes liability.
3
Apply the same principle to the fasting cases
The text extends the ruling: a traveler who breaks his fast and dies before settling (iqamah) does not need a will; similarly, a sick person who breaks his fast and dies before recovery. In both cases, the excuse (travel or illness) persisted until death, so the missed fast is not a liability.
The traveler's fast was excused from the start; the sick person's fast was broken due to illness, and recovery never occurred.
4
Distinguish from cases where qada was possible
If the person had the ability to make up the missed acts (e.g., recovery after illness, settling after travel) but died before doing so, then a will for fidyah or qada would be required. The key differentiator is whether the excuse persisted until death.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (فى اسقاط الصلوة والصوم)

اذا مات المريض ولم يقدر على الصلوة بالايماء لا يلزمه الايصاء بها وان قلت وكذا الصوم

ترجمه : (۲۹۸) اگر مریض مرنے لگے اور اشارے پر نماز پڑھنے پر قدرت نہ ہو تو اس کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ، چاہے تھوڑی سی نماز کیوں نہ ہو ۔ ایسے ہی مسافر نے اقامت سے پہلے اور بیمار نے درست ہونے سے پہلے روزہ توڑا ہو [ تو وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے]

تشریح : یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ اللہ نے نماز روزہ نہ کرنے کی گنجائش دی ہو اور اس پر وہ رہ گئی اس کے فدے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ تو پہلے ہی سے معاف تھی ۔ یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] بیمار اس حال میں تھا کہ اشارے سے بھی نماز پڑھنے کی طاقت نہیں تھی ، اس لئے ایک دن رات سے کم نماز ہو تو یہ واجب تو ہے لیکن بعد میں ادا کریں گے،اب اسی حال میں انتقال ہو گیا تو اس کا فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ اس وقت ادا کرنا واجب ہوتا جبکہ اس کو صحت ہوتی اور وہ ہوئی نہیں اس لئے اس کے ذمے واجب بھی نہیں ہے، اس لئے وصیت کرنا بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ [۲] مسافر نے سفر میں روزہ توڑ دیا اور ابھی اقامت نہیں ہوئی تھی کہ انتقال ہو گیا تو اس پر اس روزے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے ۔ [۳] مریض نے بیماری کی حالت میں روزہ توڑ دیا اور صحت نہیں ہوئی تو وصیت واجب نہیں۔
Chapter: On Dropping of Prayer and Fasting. If a sick person dies and was unable to pray even by gesture, he is not required to make a will for it, even if few; likewise for fasting. Translation: ... [detailed Urdu]
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling that a sick person who dies while unable to perform prayer even by gesture does not need to make a will for compensation (fidyah). The reason is that the obligation was suspended due to inability, and since health never returned, the obligation was not established. Similarly, a traveler who broke his fast before settling and died, or a sick person who broke his fast before recovery, does not need to make a will for compensation. The principle is that what is excused by a valid concession does not become a debt.

Key Terms
ايصاء (isa'): Making a will or testament, here specifically to pay fidyah for missed prayers or fasts.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation paid for missed fasts (or prayers) when unable to make them up.
اسقاط (isqat): Shedding or dropping of an obligation due to a valid excuse.

C) He must make up the fast after death through a relative.

Key Takeaway
A missed prayer or fast due to a valid shari'ah excuse that persists until death does not require a will for fidyah in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Making Up Prayers for the Insane or Unconscious
States the ruling on making up missed prayers due to insanity or unconsciousness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for prayers missed due to insanity or unconsciousness and apply the duration threshold (one day and night) to determine the obligation.

Core Idea
No qada for missed prayers if unconsciousness or insanity exceeds one day and night.

This lesson presents a key Hanafi ruling regarding the obligation to make up prayers missed due to loss of legal responsibility (ghayr mukallaf). The text from the matn establishes a clear threshold: five prayers (approximately one day and night) and beyond absolves the person of qada, while fewer than five require making up. This ruling is based on prophetic hadith and the principle of removing hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The ruling covers prayers missed due to insanity (junun) or unconsciousness (ighma). These states remove full legal responsibility (taklif).
2
Determine the duration
The key factor is the length of time the person remained in that state. The threshold is one full day and night (equivalent to five obligatory prayers).
If the duration is exactly one day and night, it counts as five prayers; more than that triggers the leniency.
3
Apply the ruling
If the person missed fewer than five prayers (< one day/night), qada is wajib. If five or more prayers were missed, no qada is required.
The ruling applies equally to both insanity and unconsciousness.
4
Examine the evidence
The hadith from Aisha (RA) quotes the Prophet (PBUH): 'There is no making up for any of that, except that he becomes unconscious during his prayer and regains consciousness while its time remains, then he prays it.' This is supplemented by the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
The evidence is zanni al-thubut but accepted in the madhhab.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Unlike the Hanafi school, the Shafi'i school generally requires qada for all missed prayers regardless of duration. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on differing interpretations of the same hadith.
The Hanafi position relies on the implicit exemption in the hadith and the principle of raf' al-haraj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل اسقاط الصلوة ولو كان موميا (۱۶۹ ومن جُنّ او اغمى عليه خمس صلوات قضى ولو اكثر لا . تشريح : ایک دن رات سے زیادہ بیہوش رہا ہو، یا مجنون رہا ہو اس کو قضا نہ کرے، اور اس سے کم رہا ہو تو اس کی نماز قضا کرے وجه : (ا) عن القاسم أنه سأل عائشة عن الرجل يغمى عليه فيترك الصلوة اليوم و اليومين وأكثر من ذالک ، فقالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : ليس بشيء من ذالك قضاء الا أن يغمى عليه في صلاته فيفيق و هو في وقتها فيصليها - (سنن بھتی، باب اسمی علیہ یفیق بعد ذهاب الوقتين فلا یکون علیه قضوهما، ج اول ص ۵۷۱ نمبر ۱۸۲۰) (۲) ایک دن سے زیادہ نماز قضا ہوئی ہو اور اس کو ادا کروائیں تو مریض کو تکلیف ہوگی اس لئے (۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال : كان يقول في المغمى عليه : اذا أغمى عليه يوم و ليلة أعاد و اذا كان اكثر من ذالك لم يعد ۔ ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما یعید انمی علیه من الصلوة ، ج ثانی ہیں اے نمبر ۶۵۹ مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب صلوة المريض على الدابة وصلوة المغمی علیہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۷ نمبر ۴۱۶۵ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ایک دن رات کے اندر ہو تو اسکو قضاء کمرے اور اس سے زیادہ ہو تو قضاء نہ کرے۔
Chapter on dropping of prayer: Even if he was [؟] (169) and whoever became insane or unconscious, for five prayers he makes up, and if more, he does not. Explanation: If one remained unconscious for more than a day and night, or remained insane, he does not make up; and if less than that, he makes up the prayers. Evidence: (1) From Al-Qasim that he asked Aisha about a man who becomes unconscious and misses prayer for a day, two days, or more. She said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no making up for any of that, except that he becomes unconscious during his prayer and regains consciousness while its time remains, then he prays it.' (2) Because if more than a day's prayers were missed and he were to perform them, it would cause hardship to the patient. (3) In the saying of the Tabi'i: Ibrahim said about the unconscious person: 'If he becomes unconscious for a day and a night, he repeats; if more than that, he does not repeat.' In this effect, it says that if it is within a day and night, he makes it up; if more, he does not.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn regarding the obligation of making up prayers for a person who was insane (junun) or unconscious (ighma). The core ruling is that if such a person misses five prayers (i.e., approximately one day and night's worth) or more, they are absolved from making them up. If they miss fewer than five, they must make them up. The commentary provides proof: a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) states that no qada is required for prayers missed due to unconsciousness except if one becomes unconscious during a prayer and regains consciousness in its time. Additionally, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i supports the distinction of one day and night. This ruling is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The Hanafi school applies this ruling strictly: the threshold is one full day and night (five prayers). If the duration is less, qada is obligatory. The madhhab does not differentiate between insanity and unconsciousness in this ruling.

Key Terms
جُنّ (junun): Insanity or madness that renders a person legally irresponsible (ghayr mukallaf).
اغمي عليه (ughmiya 'alayh): Unconsciousness or fainting, similar to insanity in its effect on the obligation of prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has elapsed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person remains unconscious for two full days and nights (missing ten prayers), according to the Hanafi school, is he required to make up those prayers?
A) Yes, all ten prayers must be made up.
B) No, because he missed more than five prayers.
C) Only if he was conscious during some of the time.
D) He must make up only the prayers of the first day.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, prolonged insanity or unconsciousness (one day/night or more) absolves the obligation to make up missed prayers, based on prophetic hadith and the principle of removing hardship.

Ruling on Will for Missed Prayers and Fasts of a Deceased Sick Person or Traveler
Rulings on conditions for wajib will and fidyah for missed prayers/fasts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a will for fidyah is wajib or not wajib for a deceased person who missed prayers or fasts due to sickness or travel.

Core Idea
Fidyah is only wajib for missed acts the deceased was able to perform before death; no will if death occurred before qada obligation.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi rulings on making a will (wasiyyah) for missed prayers and fasts by a deceased person who was sick or traveling. The key principle is that the obligation of fidyah depends on whether the deceased had a chance to make up the missed acts before death. We will examine three scenarios and the general rule for when a will is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify scenarios with no will obligation
List the three cases where no will is required: (1) sick person unable to pray even by gesture, (2) traveler who broke fast and died before residency, (3) sick person who broke fast and died before recovery.
In all three, death occurred before qada became due.
2
Understand when will is wajib
If the deceased had some ability to perform the missed acts (e.g., recovered briefly or took up residency), then those missed acts become wajib to make up; a will for fidyah is wajib if he died before performing them.
Only the portion he was able to perform requires a will.
3
Note the fidyah amount
For each missed prayer or fast, the fidyah is half a sa' of wheat (or its value), to be given from one-third of the estate.
This applies to both salah and sawm, and witr is included.
4
Recognize voluntary payment
If no will was made, the guardian or anyone else may voluntarily pay the fidyah on behalf of the deceased; this is permissible but not obligatory.
This payment is considered tabarru'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (فى اسقاط الصلوة والصوم (۲۹۸) اذا مات المريض ولم يقدر على الصلوة بالايماء لا يلزمه الايصاء بها وان قلت وكذا الصوم تشريح : یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ اللہ نے نماز روزہ نہ کرنے کی گنجائش دی ہو اور اس پر وہ رہ گئی اس کے فدے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ تو پہلے ہی سے معاف تھی ۔ یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] بیمار اس حال میں تھا کہ اشارے سے بھی نماز پڑھنے کی طاقت نہیں تھی ، اس لئے ایک دن رات سے کم نماز ہو تو یہ واجب تو ہے لیکن بعد میں ادا کریں گے،اب اسی حال میں انتقال ہو گیا تو اس کا فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ اس وقت ادا کرنا واجب ہوتا جبکہ اس کو صحت ہوتی اور وہ ہوئی نہیں اس لئے اس کے ذمے واجب بھی نہیں ہے، اس لئے وصیت کرنا بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ [۲] مسافر نے سفر میں روزہ توڑ دیا اور ابھی اقامت نہیں ہوئی تھی کہ انتقال ہو گیا تو اس پر اس روزے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے ۔ [۳] مریض نے بیماری کی حالت میں روزہ توڑا اور ابھی صحت نہیں ہوئی کہ اس روزے کو ادا کرتا ، اور انتقال ہو گیا تو اس روزے کی وصیت واجب نہیں ہے۔ وجه : اس آیت میں ہے کہ جو مریض ہو یا سفر پر ہو اس کو روزہ مؤخر کرنے کی گنجائش ہے۔ أياما معدودات فمن كان منكم مريضا او على سفر فعدة من ايام اخر - ( آیت ۱۸۴، سورة البقرة ٢) لغت : ان قلت: سے اشارہ ہے کہ ایک دن رات سے کم نمازیں ہوں تو بھی وہ مؤخر ہیں، اور ایک دن رات سے زیادہ ہوں تو پہلے گزرا کہ بعض کے نزدیک وہ معاف ہیں اس کی قضا بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ ان افطر فيه المسافر والمريض وماتا قبل الاقامة والصحة (۶۹۹) وعليه الوصية بما قدر عليه وبقى بذمته تشريح : مسافر یا مریض جتنے روزے اور نماز پر قادر ہوا اتنے کی وصیت کرنا ضروری ہے، مثلا بیمار کی پانچ نمازیں چھوٹی تھیں اور تین نماز ادا کرنے کا موقع ملا تو تین نماز کے فدیہ دینے کی وصیت کرنا واجب ہے ، باقی دو کی نہیں ۔ وتر چونکہ حنفیہ کے نزدیک واجب ہے اس لئے اس کے بدلے بھی فدیہ دے۔ (۷۰۰) فيخرج عنه وليه من ثلث ما ترك الصوم كل يوم ولصلوة كل وقت حتى الوتر نصف تشريح : میت نے جو مال چھوڑا ہے ولی اس میں سے تہائی مال سے نکالے گا۔ ہر دن کے روزے کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں یا اس کی قیمت ، اسی طرح ہر ایک وقت کی نماز کے بدلے آدھا صاع گیہوں، بلکہ وتر کے بدلے بھی آدھا صاع گیہوں یا اس کی قیمت فدیہ دے۔ وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو تو فدیہ دے۔ وعلى الذين يطيقونه فدية طعام مسكين فمن تطوع خيرا فهو خير له و ان تصوموا خير لكم ان كنتم تعلمون ( آيت ۱۸۴، سورة البقرة ٢)(۲) اثر میں ہے . سمع ابن عباس يقول وعلى الذين يطيقونه فدية طعام مسكين قال ابن عباس لیست بمنسوخة ، هو الشيخ الكبير و المرأة الكبيرة لا يستطيعان أن يصوما ، فليطعمان مكان كل يوم مسكينا . ( بخاری شریف ، باب قولہ تعالی ایا ما معدودات فمن کان منکم مریضا الخ، ص ۷۶۶ نمبر ۴۵۰۵ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب من قال هی مثبته شیخ الکبیلی ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۲۳۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ روز و نہ رکھ سکتا ہو تو اس کے بدلے مسکین کو کھانا کھلائے ، اور نماز کو بھی اسی پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے۔ (۷۰۱) وإن لم يوص و أخرج عنه تبرعا جاز تشريح : اگر مرنے والے نے وصیت کی ہوتب تو ولی پر اس کا ادا کرنا واجب ہے لیکن اگر اس نے وصیت نہیں کی اور ولی نے اس کی طرف سے تبرعا ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔
Chapter: On dropping of prayer and fasting. (298) If a sick person dies and was not able to pray even by gesture, he is not obligated to make a will for it, even if few, and likewise for fasting. Explanation: These issues are based on the principle that Allah has granted a concession for not praying/fasting, so if it remains unperformed, making a will for its ransom is not obligatory because it was already forgiven. There are three issues here: [1] The sick person was in a state where he could not even pray by gesture, so if the missed prayers are less than a day and night, they are wajib but will be made up later. If he dies in that state, there is no need to will for ransom because it would have been wajib only if he recovered. Since he didn't, it was not obligatory upon him, so will is not obligatory. [2] A traveler broke his fast while traveling and died before taking up residence, so making a will for that fast is not obligatory. [3] A sick person broke his fast while sick and died before recovering and performing it, so will for that fast is not obligatory. Evidence: In the verse: 'O you who believe, fasting is prescribed for you... (up to) but if any of you is ill or on a journey, a number of other days.' (2:184) Lexicon: The phrase 'if you say' indicates that if prayers are less than a day and night, they are deferred; if more than a day and night, they are forgiven according to some, and their qada is not obligatory. If the traveler and sick person broke their fast and died before residency and health, (699) and upon him is the will for what he was able to do and remained in his liability. Explanation: The traveler or sick person must make a will for the amount of fasts and prayers he was able to perform. For example, a patient missed five prayers but had the chance to perform three, so he must will to give ransom for three; the remaining two are not required. Since witr is wajib according to the Hanafis, ransom is given for it as well. (700) So his guardian should take out from one-third of what he left: for each day of fasting half a sa' of wheat, and for each prayer time up to witr half a sa'. Explanation: The guardian takes from one-third of the estate left by the deceased. For each day of fasting, half a sa' of wheat or its value; likewise for each prayer time, half a sa' of wheat, even for witr. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'And on those who are able to fast, a ransom of feeding a poor person...' (2:184) (2) The athar: Ibn Abbas heard and said: 'It is not abrogated; it is for the old man and old woman who cannot fast, so they must feed a poor person for each day.' This hadith indicates that one who cannot fast should feed a poor person, and prayer is analogized to it. (701) And if he did not make a will and [someone] gives it voluntarily on his behalf, it is permissible. Explanation: If the deceased made a will, the guardian is obliged to execute it. But if he did not make a will and the guardian voluntarily gives it on his behalf, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings (mas'ala 298, 699, 700, 701) regarding the obligation of making a will for missed prayers and fasts when a person dies before being able to make them up. The key principle is that if the obligation to pray/fast was not yet firmly established due to a valid concession (like sickness or travel), then making a will for ransom is not obligatory. Specifically: (1) A sick person who could not pray even by gesture does not need to will for those prayers, regardless of quantity. (2-3) A traveler or sick person who broke a fast and died before the end of his concession (residency or health) does not need to will for those fasts because they were not yet wajib to be made up at the time of death. However, if the person was able to perform some of the missed acts (e.g., had an opportunity to make up some prayers), he must will for those. The ransom amount is half a sa' of wheat per missed day/prayer, to be given from one-third of the estate. If no will is made, a voluntary payment by the guardian is permissible but not obligatory. The proof is from the Quran (2:184) and the hadith of Ibn Abbas applying it to those permanently unable to fast. The Hanafi school extends this to prayers by qiyas.

Key Terms
إيصاء (isa'): Making a will or bequest (wasiyyah) regarding missed religious obligations (prayer/fasting).
فدية (fidyah): Ransom or compensation paid by feeding a poor person (half sa' of wheat) for each missed fast or prayer that cannot be made up by qada.
تبرعا (tabarru'an): Voluntarily, without obligation. Here, the guardian or someone else voluntarily pays fidyah on behalf of the deceased even without a will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick person missed five prayers during a period of unconsciousness and died without regaining consciousness. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the obligation regarding fidyah?
A) Fidyah must be paid for all five prayers from one-third of the estate.
B) No fidyah is required because he was unable to pray at all.
C) Fidyah is required for the first three prayers only.
D) The guardian must pay fidyah from his own wealth.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires fidyah only for missed acts the deceased could have performed; death during a concession period generally removes the obligation to will.

Obligation of Will for Missed Fasts and Prayers
Ruling on will and fidya for missed fasts/prayers before death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making a will for missed fasts and prayers and explain the fidya amount and evidentiary basis.

Core Idea
A will for fidya of missed fasts/prayers is wajib if the deceased had opportunity to make them up; fidya is half a sa' per missed act.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a crucial scenario: a traveler or sick person who missed fasts or prayers and died before being able to make them up. The Hanafi school rules that such a person must make a will for fidya (compensation) from one-third of their estate. The fidya amount is half a sa' of wheat per missed fast or prayer, including witr. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm: making a will for missed fasts/prayers that one was able to perform is wajib. The guardian must execute the will from one-third of the estate.
The ruling is conditional on the deceased having had an opportunity to make up the missed acts.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (2:184) is cited: 'And upon those who are able [but do not fast] a fidya of feeding a poor person.' This verse is considered not abrogated and applies to permanent inability.
The Hanafi school extends this via qiyas to missed prayers.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The general permission for fidya in the verse is taken as a proof for compensation when fasting is not possible. The hadith of Ibn Abbas confirms the verse's application to those who cannot fast permanently.
Prayer is analogized to fasting due to the shared meaning of inability.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may not require fidya for missed prayers or may limit it to fasting only. The Hanafi inclusion of witr is because witr is wajib in the school.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, other schools might not pay fidya for prayers.

Chapter of Compensation for Prayer. Thamaratun Najah Vol 2: If the traveler and the sick person break the fast therein and die before reaching residence and health, (699) and upon him is the will for what he was able to do and remained in his liability. (700) So his guardian extracts from one-third of what he left: for fasting each day and for prayer each time, even witr, half a sa' of wheat or its value. ... Explanation: ... He broke the fast and health did not occur so that he could perform that fast, and he passed away, then a will for that fast is not obligatory. Evidence: In this verse, whoever is sick or on a journey has leeway to postpone the fast. ... (Translation and commentary follow)
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling from the chapter on isqat al-salah (compensation for missed acts of worship). The text addresses the situation of a traveler or sick person who breaks their fast (i.e., does not fast during Ramadan due to travel or illness) and then dies before they become resident or healthy, before they had a chance to make up those missed fasts. The ruling states: (699) The deceased must make a will regarding the amount he was able to perform but still owed—i.e., if he had the opportunity to make up some fasts or prayers but did not, he must will that fidya be given for those. (700) The guardian (wali) of the deceased is to take one-third of the estate and give as fidya half a sa' of wheat or its value for each missed day of fasting and for each missed prayer time, including the witr prayer. The Urdu commentary elaborates: if a sick person missed five prayers but only had time to make up three, he must make a will for the three he could have performed, not the two he could not. Witr is included because in the Hanafi school it is wajib (obligatory). The proofs are Quran 2:184, which allows fidya for those unable to fast, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the verse is not abrogated and applies to the old who cannot fast, and prayer is analogized (qiyas) to fasting.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will made by the deceased regarding fidya for missed fasts/prayers, obligating the guardian to pay from one-third of the estate.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation payment of half a sa' of wheat or its value for each missed fast/prayer.
ولی (wali): The guardian or executor of the deceased, responsible for paying fidya from the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One quarter sa' of wheat
B) Half a sa' of wheat or its value
C) One sa' of wheat
D) Feeding one poor person one meal

Key Takeaway
A will for fidya of missed fasts/prayers is wajib if possible; fidya is half a sa' per missed act, paid from one-third of the estate.

Voluntary Fidya by Guardian Without a Will
Ruling on voluntary fidya by guardian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary fidya by the guardian in the absence of a will, and identify the hadith evidence that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Voluntary fidya by the guardian is valid even without a will — the guardian’s action fulfills the deceased’s obligation.

In the previous lessons, we learned that fidya is due for missed fasts (and prayers) if the deceased made a will. But what if there was no will? Can someone step in voluntarily? This passage clarifies that the guardian’s voluntary payment is valid, based on a hadith of Ibn Umar. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The guardian voluntarily paying fidya for the deceased without a will. The ruling: permissible (mubah) and accepted on behalf of the deceased.
This is a dispensation, not an obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever dies while owing a month of fasting, let food be given on his behalf for each day for a poor person.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'falyut'im' (let him feed) indicates permission for the guardian to act on behalf of the deceased. The generality of the hadith covers both cases where a will exists and where it does not.
The Hanafi school uses the hadith as a general permission.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may restrict this to fasting only, while Hanafi extends it to missed prayers by qiyas (analogy).
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether voluntary fidya for prayers is valid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that voluntary payment by the guardian is valid and accepted for both fasts and prayers, as per Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on isqat al-salah. It presents the ruling (701): If the deceased did not make a will (i.e., did not instruct the guardian to pay fidya), and the guardian voluntarily pays the fidya from his own side or from the estate, it is permissible and accepted on behalf of the deceased. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: whoever dies owing a month of fasting, let food be given on his behalf for each day for a poor person. This establishes that voluntary payment by the guardian is valid. The passage then provides a detailed weight table to clarify the measure of half a sa' in modern units: one sa' = 8 ratl ≈ 3.538 kg ≈ 5.88 liters; half a sa' = 4 ratl ≈ 1.769 kg ≈ 2.94 liters. The conclusion summarizes that half a sa' is the amount of sadaqat al-fitr as well, and fidya can be given in wheat or its value.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): Voluntary act of giving fidya without being obligated by a will.
صاع (sa'): A dry measure of volume; here defined as 8 ratl ≈ 3.538 kg wheat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a guardian’s voluntary fidya for the deceased’s missed fasts (and by analogy prayers) is valid and accepted, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar, even without a will.

Fidya Amount and Guardian's Voluntary Payment on Behalf of Deceased
Ruling on fidya amount and guardian's voluntary payment for deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fidya amount for missed fasts and prayers according to the Hanafi school and explain the validity of a guardian's voluntary payment without bequest.

Core Idea
One sa' of wheat per missed day, even when the guardian pays voluntarily without a bequest.

When a person dies with missed fasts or prayers that they could not make up, the Hanafi school establishes fidya as a wajib compensation. This lesson covers the required amount (one sa' of wheat or its value) and the important rule that the guardian (wali) can pay it voluntarily from his own wealth, thereby discharging the deceased's obligation, even if no bequest was made. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar (RA).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Amount
State the fidya amount: one sa' of wheat or its value. Understand that this applies to missed fasts and prayers.
Hanafi definition: sa' is 8 ratls, approx. 3.538 liters.
2
Examine the Condition of Bequest
Normally fidya is taken from the estate only if the deceased bequeathed it. The text adds a permissive case: if the guardian pays voluntarily without a bequest, it is valid.
The phrase 'وان لم يوص' indicates absence of bequest.
3
Analyze the Dalil (Proof)
The hadith: 'Whoever dies and has a month of fasting, let him feed a poor person for every day on his behalf.' Identify the imperative 'فليطعم' as indicating obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The imperative is understood as wajib per Hanafi principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub'.
4
Apply the Hanafi Hukm
Conclude that fidya is wajib per missed day, and the guardian's voluntary payment (tabarru') fulfills the obligation.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل اسقاط الصلوة صاع من بر او قيمته (۱(۷۰) وان لم يوص وتبرع عنه وليه جاز اپنی جانب سے تبرع کیا اور ادا کیا تب بھی میت کی جانب سے ادا کبھی جائے گی۔ وجه: (ا) عـن ابـن عـمـر عـن الـنبـي الله قـال مـن مـات و عـلـيـه صـيـام شـهـر فليطعم عنه مكان كل يوم مسكينا. ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في الكفارة ،ص۱۸۲، نمبر ۱۸ے رسن بیہقی ، باب من قال اذ افرط في القضاء بعد الا مکان حتی مات الخ، ج رابع ، ص ۴۲۴، نمبر ۸۲۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ میت کی جانب سے ولی نے ادا کیا تو ادا ہو جائے گا۔
Chapter on Dropping of Prayer: A sa' of wheat or its value. And if he did not bequeath and his guardian donated on his behalf, it is valid—even if he donated and paid from his own side, it will be considered as fulfillment on behalf of the deceased. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever dies and has a month of fasting, then let him feed a poor person for every day on his behalf.' (Tirmidhi, Chapter on Kaffarah, p.182, no. [؟]; Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter on... vol.4, p.424, no.8217). This hadith indicates that when the guardian pays on behalf of the deceased, it will be fulfillment.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a proof from hadith. The chapter begins with the rule that the fidya for missed fasts and prayers is one sa' of wheat or its monetary value. The text then addresses a scenario: if the deceased did not leave a bequest (وصية) but the guardian (ولي) voluntarily donates and pays the fidya from his own wealth, this is valid and the obligation is considered fulfilled on behalf of the deceased. The proof is the hadith narrated by Ibn Umar where the Prophet ﷺ instructs feeding a poor person for each missed fast day. This indicates that financial compensation (fidya) can be given by a guardian even without a bequest. The Hanafi position is that fidya becomes wajib upon the heirs from the estate if the deceased bequeathed; otherwise, if the guardian does it voluntarily, it is accepted. The weight of a sa' is detailed later in the text (approximately 1.769 kg of wheat). This is from Zahir al-Riwayah as found in the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume measure, equivalent to approximately 1.769 kg of wheat (as per the text's calculation).
فدیہ (fidya): Compensatory payment for missed fasts or prayers when one is unable to make them up before death.
ولی (wali): Guardian or heir of the deceased, responsible for managing affairs if no bequest exists.
تبرع (tabarru'): Voluntary donation or act of charity without being legally obligated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fidya amount per missed fast according to this passage?
A) Half a sa' of barley
B) One sa' of wheat or its value
C) One mudd of dates
D) Two sa's of wheat

Key Takeaway
Fidya for missed fasts and prayers is one sa' of wheat per day; a guardian can pay voluntarily without a bequest, and it is accepted based on the hadith's imperative.

Salah — Prayer

Invalidity of Proxy Prayer and Fasting
Ruling with proof from Companion sayings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that proxy physical worship is invalid and identify the proof from the sayings of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
No one can pray or fast for another; physical worship is strictly personal.

This lesson establishes a core Hanafi principle: acts of physical worship like prayer and fasting cannot be performed by one person on behalf of another. The text provides direct evidence from the Companion Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه) and explains why proxy is invalid. Understanding this ruling distinguishes physical worship from financial worship and prepares you for the legal stratagem (hila) that follows in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the first part of the passage (702): 'ولا يصح ان يصوم ولا ان يصلى عنه'. Identify what action is being ruled invalid and who the 'anhu' refers to (the deceased).
The ruling applies to both prayer and fasting, and to any deceased person, even if the guardian intends to help.
2
Examine the classification of worship
The commentary divides worship into three types: physical, financial, and combined. Note why proxy is allowed only in financial and combined forms, not in purely physical ones.
Physical worship requires personal effort; the obligation is to exert one's own body.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The text cites two narrations from Ibn Umar. In the first, he says: 'لا يصوم احد عن احد و لكن تصدقوا عنه'. In the second: 'لا يصلين أحد عن أحد'. Understand that these clear prohibitions are the evidence for the ruling.
The proof is a qawl sahabi (saying of a companion), which is a valid source in Hanafi usul but zanni in transmission.
4
Distinguish the alternative: fidya
Ibn Umar directs to give charity (fidya) instead of proxy fasting. Note that fidya transforms the obligation from physical to financial, which can be discharged by the guardian.
Fidya is a substitute, not a proxy performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۰۲) ولا يصح ان يصوم ولا ان يصلى عنه (۷۰۳ وان لم يف ما اوصى به عما عليه يدفع ذلک المقدار للفقير فيسقط عن الميت بقدره ثم يهبه الفقير للولى ويقبضه ثم يدفعه للفقير فيسقط بقدره نوٹ : احتیاطا مہینہ 30 ۔ دن کا مانا ہے۔ اور سال 355 ۔ دن کا مانا ہے۔ اور وتر کو ملا کر دن کی 6۔ نمازیں مانی ہیں۔ نوٹ: یہ حساب احسن الفتاوی، رسالہ، بسط الباع تحقیق الصاع ، ج رابع ص ۴۱۶ سے لیا گیا ہے۔ البتہ وہاں پونے دو کیلو جو ہے میں نے احتیاط کے لئے گیہوں کر دیا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۷۰۲) اور ولی کا اس کی جانب سے نماز وروز و ادا کرنا صحیح نہیں۔ تشریح : عبادت تین قسم کی ہے [1] عبادت بدنی، جیسے نماز، روزہ۔ اس میں وہی آدمی ادا کرے جس پر فرض ہوئی ہے تا کہ اسی کو مشقت ہو۔ چنانچہ نماز اور روزہ کوئی اور ادا کرنا چاہے تو ادا نہیں کر سکتا، ہاں اس کے بدلے میں فدیہ ولی دینا چاہے تو فدیہ دے سکتا ہے، کیونکہ یہ عبادت مالی بن گئی [۲] دوسری ہے عبادت مالی ، جیسے زکوۃ اور صدقات ، کفارات ۔اس میں مشقت مال خرچ کرنے میں ہوتی ہے، اس لئے جس پر فرض ہوئی ہے اس کے حکم سے کوئی ادا کرے گا تو ادا ہو جائے گی ،مثلا زید پر زکوۃ واجب ہوئی اور اس کے حکم سے عمر نے ادا کی تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [۳] اور تیسری قسم ہے بدنی اور مالی دونوں کا مجموعہ، جیسے حج ، کہ اس میں مال بھی خرچ ہوتا ہے، اور آدمی کو احرام باندھ کر مشقت بھی برداشت کرنی پڑتی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر كان اذا سئل عن الرجل يموت و عليه صوم من رمضان أو نذر يقول : لا يصوم احد عن احد ، و لكن تصدقوا عنه من ماله للصوم لكل يوم مسكينا ۔ (سنن بیہقی، باب من قال از افرط في القضاء بعد الا مکان حتی مات الخ، ج رابع ، ص ۴۲۴، نمبر ۸۲۱۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کوئی کسی کا روزہ نہ رکھے بلکہ اس کی جانب سے فدیہ دے (۲) اس قول صحابی میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال : لا يصلين أحد عن أحد و لا يصو من أحد عن أحد ولكن ان كنت فاعلا تصدقت أو اهديت ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصدقة عن لمیت ، ج تاسع ، ص ۸، نمبر ۱۶۶۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ میت کی نماز کے بدلے میں نماز نہ پڑھے بلکہ اس کے بدلے میں فدیہ دے۔ ترجمه : (۷۰۳) اور اگر اس کی وصیت مافی الذمہ کو کافی نہ ہو تو ( حیلہ یہ کہ اتناہی فقیر کو دینے سے اس کے اندازے کے موافق اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہوگا ، پھر اسے فقیر ولی کو بخش دے کر قبضہ کرا دے پھر اسے فقیر کو دے دے تو اب اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گیا ، پھر فقیر ولی کو دے کر قبضہ کرا دے پھر ولی اسے فقیر کو دید یوے، اسی طرح وہاں تک کرتا رہے کہ میت کے ذمہ سے تمام روزے اور نماز ساقط ہو جائے۔ تشریح : میت پر اتنے روزے، اور نماز ہیں کہ انکے ترکہ میں سے تہائی نکالیں تو اس سے پورے فدئے ادا نہیں ہوتے ، تو اس
(702) And it is not valid for anyone to fast or pray on his behalf. (703) And if what he bequeathed does not suffice what is owed upon him, then he gives that amount to the poor person, so it drops from the deceased to that extent, then the poor person gifts it to the guardian and he takes possession, then he gives it to the poor person, so it drops to that extent. Note: Cautiously, a month is considered 30 days, and a year 355 days, and including witr, 6 prayers per day. Note: This calculation is taken from Ahsan al-Fatawa, Risala, Bast al-Ba' fi Tahqiq al-Sa', vol.4, p.416. However, there it was 3/4 of a kilo of wheat; I changed it to wheat out of caution. Translation: (702) And it is not valid for the guardian to pray or fast on his behalf. Explanation: Worship is of three types: [1] Physical worship, like prayer and fasting. Only the person obligated can perform it so that he bears the hardship. Thus no one else can pray or fast for him; however, the guardian may give fidya instead, because it becomes financial worship. [2] Financial worship, like zakat, sadaqat, and kaffarat. Hardship is in spending wealth, so if someone pays by the command of the obligated person, it is valid. For example, Zaid owes zakat and Umar pays by his command, it is valid. [3] Combined physical and financial worship, like Hajj, which involves spending wealth and bearing hardship of ihram. Evidence: (1) In the saying of the companion: Ibn Umar, when asked about a man who dies and owes fasts from Ramadan or a vow, used to say: 'No one should fast for another, but give charity on his behalf from his wealth for each day a poor person.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, vol.4, p.424, no.8215). This athar shows that no one should fast for another, rather give fidya. (2) Also in the saying of Ibn Umar: 'No one should pray for another, and no one should fast for another; but if you are doing something, give charity or gift.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, vol.9, p.8, no.16657). This athar shows that one should not pray for the deceased but give fidya. Translation: (703) And if his bequest is not sufficient for what is upon him, the stratagem is that he gives that amount to a poor person, so it drops from the deceased to that extent; then the poor person gifts it to the guardian and he takes possession; then he gives it to the poor person, so it drops to that extent; then the poor person gives it to the guardian and he takes possession; then the guardian gives it to the poor person. In this way he continues until all the fasts and prayers are dropped from the deceased. Explanation: The deceased has so many fasts and prayers that if one-third of his estate is taken out, it does not cover the full fidya.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First (702): It is not valid for anyone to perform physical worship (prayer or fasting) on behalf of another person, whether living or deceased. The text provides evidence from the practice of Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه), who explicitly said no one should pray or fast for another. Instead, fidya (financial compensation) can be given. This is because physical worship requires direct personal performance; the obligation is tied to the individual's ability. Fidya transforms the obligation from physical to financial, which can be discharged by the guardian. The Hanafi school classifies worship into three categories: physical (purely bodily, like salah/sawm), financial (like zakat), and combined (like hajj). Proxy is only allowed in financial and combined types under certain conditions.

Second (703): When the deceased's bequest (وصية) is insufficient to cover the fidya for all missed prayers and fasts, a legal stratagem (حيلة) is employed. The guardian gives a specific amount (e.g., one sa' of wheat) to a poor person, which clears the deceased's liability to that extent. Then the poor person gifts that same amount back to the guardian, who then gives it again to the poor person. This cycle is repeated until the entire liability is cleared. This hila is based on the principle that once the poor person owns the amount, he can freely dispose of it, including gifting it back. The guardian must ensure possession (قبض) each time. The text also includes practical notes: a month is considered 30 days, a year 355 days, and 6 prayers per day (including witr) are counted. The fidya calculation uses wheat as the standard. This hila is a recognized solution in Hanafi fiqh for cases where the estate is limited.

Key Terms
اسقاط (isqat): Dropping or removal of an obligation, here through fidya.
فدیہ (fidya): Compensatory payment for missed acts of worship when incapable of performing them, valued at one sa' of wheat per act.
بدنی (badani): Physical worship that requires personal bodily exertion, like salah and sawm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the evidence from Ibn Umar, what should be done instead of proxy fasting for a deceased person?
A) Nothing; the debt is cancelled.
B) Give charity (fidya) from the deceased's wealth.
C) Perform extra fasts on behalf of the deceased.
D) The guardian should fast for the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Proxy physical worship (prayer/fasting) is invalid; only fidya (financial compensation) can be given.

Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Insufficient Fidya
Ruling with procedural description (legal stratagem)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the hila process for discharging a deceased's liability when the bequest is insufficient, and identify the condition of possession (qabd) in each transfer.

Core Idea
Repeated gifting between guardian and poor person clears debt on limited funds.

This lesson presents a practical solution (hila) when the deceased's bequest (thulth of estate) is not enough to cover all fidya. The stratagem involves repeatedly giving the same amount to a poor person and receiving it back as a gift, until the full liability is discharged. This is a recognized Hanafi mechanism, based on the principle that once the poor person owns the wealth, he may gift it back. Understanding this hila is crucial for estates with limited funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: insufficient bequest
Read the beginning of (703): 'وان لم يف ما اوصى به عما عليه'. Understand that the deceased's one-third bequest is inadequate to pay fidya for all missed obligations.
The fidya amount is one sa' per missed prayer/fast. The total debt may exceed one-third of the estate.
2
Step through the hila cycle
The text describes a cycle: (1) guardian gives amount to poor person → debt decreases by that amount; (2) poor person gifts it back to guardian; (3) guardian takes possession (qabd); (4) guardian gives again to poor person; repeat. Trace each transfer and note the effect on the deceased's liability.
Possession (qabd) is a condition for ownership transfer; the poor person must physically receive before gifting back.
3
Understand the legal rationale
The hila works because each time the poor person owns the amount, he can voluntarily gift it. The guardian is not forcing him; it is a willing transfer. This avoids suspicion of a mere paper transaction.
The hila is based on the principle of ownership and gift; it is not considered a trick to evade payment, but a legitimate means to discharge debt.
4
Calculate the required fidya
The text includes notes: month = 30 days, year = 355 days, 6 prayers per day (including witr). Multiply to get total fidya units. Compare to available bequest.
The fidya unit is one sa' of wheat. The calculation is from later Hanafi fatwa works.

This hila is a recognized solution in Hanafi fiqh for cases where the estate is limited.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome, here to clear deceased's liability with limited funds.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of an item, a necessary condition for ownership transfer in gifts.
فقیر (faqir): A poor person eligible to receive charity, defined as one who does not have nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hila described, what must happen for the guardian to receive the wealth back from the poor person?
A) The poor person must sell it back.
B) The poor person must gift it back voluntarily.
C) The guardian must take it by force.
D) The poor person must loan it to the guardian.

Key Takeaway
The hila allows clearing a larger fidya debt by repeatedly giving the same limited wealth to a poor person and receiving it back as a gift, ensuring ownership transfers each time.

Proxy Worship for the Deceased Is Invalid
States ruling that proxy worship is invalid for deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing prayers and fasts on behalf of the deceased and explain the evidence from the companion Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Physical worship cannot be delegated; only financial compensation (fidyah) clears the deceased's liability.

This passage addresses a common question: can someone pray or fast for a deceased relative who missed obligations? The Hanafi school answers clearly: no, because physical worship is personal. However, the guardian may give fidyah from the deceased's wealth. Let's examine the ruling, its classification of worship types, and the proof from Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing prayers or fasts on behalf of a deceased person. The ruling is that it is invalid (la yasihh).
The passage uses 'ولا يصح' indicating legal invalidity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of Ibn Umar (ra) recorded in Sunan Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, explicitly negating proxy fasting and praying, and directing to give charity (fidyah).
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation 'لا يصوم أحد عن أحد' shows prohibition; the command 'تصدقوا عنه' shows the alternative is financial.
The imperative indicates obligation (wujub) of fidyah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools permit proxy worship; Hanafis restrict to financial compensation because physical worship requires personal exertion.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the companion's qawl, which is preferred over general analogies. The classification of worship into physical/financial/combined supports the ruling.
The tarjih is implicit in the passage's structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل اسقاط الصلوة
(۷۰۲) ولا يصح ان يصوم ولا ان يصلى عنه
نوٹ : احتیاطا مہینہ 30 ۔ دن کا مانا ہے۔ اور سال 355 ۔ دن کا مانا ہے۔ اور وتر کو ملا کر دن کی 6۔ نمازیں مانی ہیں۔ نوٹ: یہ حساب احسن الفتاوی، رسالہ، بسط الباع تحقیق الصاع ، ج رابع ص ۴۱۶ سے لیا گیا ہے۔ البتہ وہاں پونے دو کیلو جو ہے میں نے احتیاط کے لئے گیہوں کر دیا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۰۲) اور ولی کا اس کی جانب سے نماز وروز و ادا کرنا صحیح نہیں۔
تشریح : عبادت تین قسم کی ہے [1] عبادت بدنی، جیسے نماز، روزہ۔ اس میں وہی آدمی ادا کرے جس پر فرض ہوئی ہے تا کہ اسی کو مشقت ہو۔ چنانچہ نماز اور روزہ کوئی اور ادا کرنا چاہے تو ادا نہیں کر سکتا، ہاں اس کے بدلے میں فدیہ ولی دینا چاہے تو فدیہ دے سکتا ہے، کیونکہ یہ عبادت مالی بن گئی [۲] دوسری ہے عبادت مالی ، جیسے زکوۃ اور صدقات ، کفارات ۔اس میں مشقت مال خرچ کرنے میں ہوتی ہے، اس لئے جس پر فرض ہوئی ہے اس کے حکم سے کوئی ادا کرے گا تو ادا ہو جائے گی ،مثلا زید پر زکوۃ واجب ہوئی اور اس کے حکم سے عمر نے ادا کی تو ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ [۳] اور تیسری قسم ہے بدنی اور مالی دونوں کا مجموعہ، جیسے حج ، کہ اس میں مال بھی خرچ ہوتا ہے، اور آدمی کو احرام باندھ کر مشقت بھی برداشت کرنی پڑتی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ ان ابن عمر كان اذا سئل عن الرجل يموت و عليه صوم من رمضان أو نذر يقول : لا يصوم احد عن احد ، و لكن تصدقوا عنه من ماله للصوم لكل يوم مسكينا ۔ (سنن بیہقی، باب من قال از افرط في القضاء بعد الا مکان حتی مات الخ، ج رابع ، ص ۴۲۴، نمبر ۸۲۱۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ کوئی کسی کا روزہ نہ رکھے بلکہ اس کی جانب سے فدیہ دے (۲) اس قول صحابی میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال : لا يصلين أحد عن أحد و لا يصو من أحد عن أحد ولكن ان كنت فاعلا تصدقت أو اهديت ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الصدقة عن لمیت ، ج تاسع ، ص ۸، نمبر ۱۶۶۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ میت کی نماز کے بدلے میں نماز نہ پڑھے بلکہ اس کے بدلے میں فدیہ دے۔
Chapter on Dropping of Prayers. (702) It is not valid that one fasts nor that one prays on his behalf. Note: Cautiously, a month is taken as 30 days and a year as 355 days, and including witr, there are 6 prayers per day. This calculation is taken from Ahsan al-Fatawa, Risala, Bast al-Ba' Tahqiq al-Sa', Volume 4, p. 416. However, there it is 1.75 kg of barley; I have changed it to wheat out of caution. Translation: (702) It is not correct for the guardian to perform prayers and fasts on his behalf. Explanation: Worship is of three types: [1] Physical worship, like prayer and fasting. The person upon whom it is obligatory must perform it so that he may experience the hardship. Thus, if someone else wants to perform prayer and fasting, he cannot; yes, the guardian may give fidyah in its place, because it becomes financial worship. [2] Financial worship, like zakat, sadaqat, and kafarat. Hardship is in spending wealth, so if someone else performs it by the order of the one upon whom it is obligatory, it will be valid. For example, Zaid owes zakat and 'Umar pays it with his permission, it will be valid. [3] The third type is combined physical and financial, like hajj, in which wealth is spent and one also bears hardship by wearing ihram. Evidence: (1) In this companion's statement: 'Ibn 'Umar, when asked about a man who dies and owes fasts of Ramadan or a vow, said: No one fasts for another, but give charity on his behalf from his wealth for the fast, for each day one poor person.' (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on 'If one exceeded in making up after being able until he died', vol. 4, p. 424, no. 8215) This report states that no one should fast for another, but rather give fidyah on his behalf. (2) Also in this companion's statement: 'Ibn 'Umar said: No one should pray for another, nor fast for another, but if you are doing it, give charity or gift.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on charity for the deceased, vol. 9, p. 8, no. 16657) This report states that instead of prayer for the deceased, give fidyah.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a ruling accompanied by proof. It opens the chapter on dropping prayers (isqat al-salat). The core ruling: it is legally invalid (la yasihh) for anyone—specifically the wali (guardian)—to perform the deceased's missed prayers or fasts. The commentary divides worship into three types: purely physical (like salah and sawm), purely financial (zakat, sadaqat, kaffarat), and combined (hajj). Physical worship cannot be delegated because its purpose is the personal exertion; financial worship can be delegated with permission; combined worship requires both the performer's presence and financial means. The proofs are two athar (sayings) of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (ra). In the first, he explicitly rejects proxy fasting and prescribes giving charity (fidyah) from the deceased's wealth. In the second, he expands the ruling to prayers as well. These are authoritative for Hanafis as qawl sahabi. The note about 30-day months and 355-day years is a cautionary calculation for the amount of fidyah due.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation payment for missed obligatory acts of worship (prayer/fasting) due to incapacity.
ولی (wali): Guardian of the deceased, usually the heir or executor responsible for fulfilling the deceased's obligations.
اسقاط (isqat): The process of dropping or discharging an obligation (here, of prayers) from the deceased's liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that proxy prayer is invalid?
A) Quranic verse 35:18
B) Hadith of Ibn Umar
C) Consensus of the four schools
D) Qiyas on zakat

Key Takeaway
Physical worship (prayer, fasting) cannot be performed by proxy; only financial compensation (fidyah) clears the deceased's liability.

The Hila for Insufficient Fidyah Bequest
Describes a legal stratagem when bequest is insufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hila for insufficient fidyah bequest and identify its conditions and validity.

Core Idea
When the deceased's fidyah bequest is insufficient, a permissible legal stratagem multiplies coverage by recycling the same gift.

A deceased person may owe fidyah for missed prayers and fasts, but the one-third of the estate set aside for bequest might be too small. The Hanafi school provides a practical mechanism: a hila (legal stratagem) using repeated gifts between the guardian and a poor person. This lesson breaks down the method and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The deceased has outstanding obligations (fidyah for salah and sawm) but the bequeathable one-third of the estate is insufficient. The goal is to discharge as much liability as possible.
The bequest is limited to one-third; if the estate is small, it may not cover all fidyah.
2
Understand the hila cycle
The available amount is given to a poor person (faqir). That person then gifts it back to the wali (guardian) with full possession. The wali gives it again to the poor person. Each cycle counts as a separate payment, accumulating towards the total fidyah.
Each transfer must be a complete gift (hibah) with physical or constructive possession (qabd).
3
Identify the conditions
The hila is valid only if: 1) the poor person is eligible, 2) each gift is complete with transfer of ownership, 3) the wali acts with integrity, 4) the intention is to discharge the deceased's liability, not to create a loop for other purposes.
The hila is permissible (ja'iz) and not deceitful because it achieves a legitimate goal through permissible means.
4
Work through the example
If the deceased owes 100 kg fidyah and only 20 kg is available, the cycle is repeated five times (20 kg × 5 = 100 kg). After each cycle, the wali must ensure the poor giver receives and returns the goods.
The example in the text uses wheat; any edible or valuable item of equivalent value may be used.
5
Recognize the school's position
This hila is accepted in Hanafi fatwa (fatawa mutakhkhirin). No specific hadith supports it, but it is a reasoned device (hila) to avoid hardship.
Other schools may not accept such a stratagem; the Hanafi school permits it based on qiyas and istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۰۳) وان لم يف ما اوصى به عما عليه يدفع ذلک المقدار للفقير فيسقط عن الميت بقدره ثم يهبه الفقير للولى ويقبضه ثم يدفعه للفقير فيسقط بقدره ثم يهبه الفقير للولى ويقبضه ثم يدفعه الولى للفقير وهكذا حتى يسقط ما كان على الميت من صلوة وصيام
ترجمه : (۷۰۳) اور اگر اس کی وصیت مافی الذمہ کو کافی نہ ہو تو ( حیلہ یہ کہ اتناہی فقیر کو دینے سے اس کے اندازے کے موافق اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہوگا ، پھر اسے فقیر ولی کو بخش دے کر قبضہ کرا دے پھر اسے فقیر کو دے دے تو اب اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گیا ، پھر فقیر ولی کو دے کر قبضہ کرا دے پھر ولی اسے فقیر کو دید یوے، اسی طرح وہاں تک کرتا رہے کہ میت کے ذمہ سے تمام روزے اور نماز ساقط ہو جائے۔
تشریح : میت پر اتنے روزے، اور نماز ہیں کہ انکے ترکہ میں سے تہائی نکالیں تو اس سے پورے فدئے ادا نہیں ہوتے ، تو اس کے لئے حیلے کی شکل نکالی ہے ، ہو سکتا ہے کہ اللہ تعالی اس سے اس کو معاف کر دے۔ البتہ اس کے لئے حدیث نہیں ملی۔ مثلا ایک سو کیلو [100] میت پر فدیہ ہے ، اور میت کی تہائی مال صرف 20 کیلوگیہوں ہے۔ تو یہ 20 فقیر کو دے دے۔ پھر فقیر اس 20 کیلو کو ولی کو دے دے اور اس کو پورا مالک بنا دے۔ اب ولی دوبارہ اس 20 کیلو کو فقیر کو دیکر اس کو مالک بنا دے تو گویا کہ 40 کیلو فدیہ میت کے ذمے سے ساقط ہوا، پھر یہ 20 کیلو فقیر ولی کو دے دے اور اس کو پورا مالک بنادے۔ اور پھر ولی یہ 20 کیلو فقیر کو دے دے، تو گویا کہ 60 کیلوفدیہ میت کے ذمے سے ساقط ہوا، اس طرح بار بار کر کے 100 کیلوفدیہ ادا کر دے۔
(703) And if what he bequeathed does not suffice for what is upon him, he gives that amount to the poor person, and it drops from the deceased to that extent. Then the poor person gifts it to the guardian and takes possession, then the guardian gives it to the poor person, and it drops to that extent. Then the poor person gifts to the guardian and takes possession, then the guardian gives it to the poor person, and so on until all that was upon the deceased of prayers and fasts drops. Translation: (703) And if his bequest does not suffice for what is on his liability, then the stratagem is that he gives that much to the poor person, and it drops from his liability according to the measure. Then the poor person gifts it to the guardian and the guardian takes possession, then he gives it to the poor person, so now it drops from his liability. Then the poor person gives to the guardian and the guardian takes possession, then the guardian gives it to the poor person, and so on until all the fasts and prayers of the deceased are dropped. Explanation: The deceased has so many fasts and prayers that if one takes one-third from his estate, the full fidyah is not paid. So a stratagem has been devised for this. It is hoped that Allah may forgive him through it. However, no hadith was found for it. For example, the deceased owes fidyah of 100 kg, and his one-third wealth is only 20 kg of wheat. So he gives this 20 to a poor person. Then the poor person gives the 20 kg to the guardian and makes him full owner. Now the guardian gives the 20 kg to the poor person again and makes him owner, so it is as if 40 kg fidyah has dropped from the deceased's liability. Then this 20 kg the poor person gives to the guardian and makes him full owner, and then the guardian gives the 20 kg to the poor person, so it is as if 60 kg fidyah has dropped. Thus by repeating, he pays the 100 kg fidyah.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a scenario where the deceased's bequest (the one-third of the estate) is insufficient to cover the fidyah for all missed prayers and fasts. The ruling prescribes a cycle: give the available amount to a poor person (faqir), who then gifts it back to the wali (guardian) with full ownership, allowing the wali to give it again. Each complete cycle counts as a new payment, thereby multiplying the effective fidyah. The example clarifies: if 20 kg of wheat is available and the total fidyah is 100 kg, repeating the cycle five times (20 kg × 5 cycles) achieves the full amount. The text notes that no specific hadith supports this method, but it is a device (hila) that scholars have formulated, hoping for divine acceptance. The wali must ensure each transfer is a complete gift (hibah) with possession (qabd) to make it valid. This is a practical solution within Hanafi fiqh for discharging the deceased's liability when assets are limited.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem or device that achieves a legitimate goal through permissible means, here to maximize fidyah coverage.
فقیر (faqir): A poor person eligible to receive fidyah or charity.
ولی (wali): Guardian of the deceased responsible for managing the estate and fulfilling obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The poor person must be a relative of the deceased.
B) Each transfer must be a complete gift with possession.

D) The deceased must have stated in the will that a hila is allowed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila allows the wali to recycle a small bequest through repeated gifts to multiply the fidyah coverage, provided each transfer is a complete gift with possession.
