Fidyah Aggregation: One Poor Person for Many Prayers
Ruling on giving multiple fidyahs to a single poor person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving multiple fidyahs to one poor person and distinguish it from kaffarat yamin using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Fidyah is financial compensation; kaffarat yamin requires actual feeding — different legal natures yield different distribution rules.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh between fidyah (compensation for missed prayers/fasts) and kaffarat yamin (expiation for a broken oath). Although both involve giving food, the school holds that fidyah can be aggregated to a single poor person while kaffarat must be distributed to ten individuals. The difference stems from the Quranic texts and the nature of the obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act and its ruling: giving fidyah for many prayers to one poor person is permissible (ja'iz).
The ruling is explicit in the source: 'وَيَجُوزُ إِعْطَاءُ فِدْيَةِ صَلَوَاتٍ لِوَاحِدٍ جُمْلَةً'
2
Identify the contrasting case
Note that the same is not allowed for kaffarat yamin (expiation of an oath).
The exception is stated: 'بِخِلَافِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ'
3
Locate the proof
The source cites Quran 2:184 for fidyah ('fidya tā'āmu miskīn') and 5:89 for kaffarat ('it'āmu 'asharat masākīn').
These are the primary textual evidences.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
For fidyah, the verse does not specify distribution, so giving ownership to one person suffices. For kaffarat, the explicit mention of 'ten poor persons' requires distribution.
Hanafi usul: umum of command for fidyah; khass (specific number) for kaffarat.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a person owes multiple fidyahs, they can give all to one poor person. For kaffarat, each oath requires feeding ten different poor persons.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۰٤) ويجوز اعطاء فدية صلوات لواحد جملةً بخلاف كفارة اليمين . والله اعلم.
ترجمه : (۷۰۴) بہت سی نمازوں کا فدیہ ایک ہی فقیر کو دینا جائز ہے، بخلاف کفارہ یمین کے [ کہ سب کفارہ ایک فقیر کو دینا جائز نہیں ہے]
تشریح : فدیہ میں آدھا صاع فقیر کو دینا ضروری ہے، کھلانا ضروری نہیں ، اس لئے کئی فدیہ کا گیہوں ایک ہی فقیر کو دے دے تو سب فدئے ادا ہو جائیں گے۔ اور قسم کے کفارے میں کھلا نا اصل ہے اور ایک مسکین کو زیادہ سے زیادہ آدھا صاع کھلا سکتا ہے اس لئے کئی مسکین کا کھانا ایک ہی کو دے دے تو ایک ہی مسکین کا کفارہ ادا ہوگا، زیادہ کا ادانہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) روزے کے فدئے میں کھانا دے دینا اصل ہے اس کا ثبوت اس آیت کے اشارے میں ہے۔ وعــلــى الـذيـن يطيقونه فدية طعام مسكين فمن تطوع خيرا فهو خير له و ان تصوموا خير لكم ان كنتم تعلمون (آیت۱۸۴، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ فدیہ کا گیہوں دے دو ۔ (۲) اور کفارہ قسم میں کھانا کھلانا اصل ہے اس کا اشارہ اس آیت میں ہے۔ لا يواخذكم الله باللغو فى ايمانكم و لكن يواخز كم بما عقدتم الايمان فكفارته اطعام عشرة مساكين من اوسط ما تطعمون اهلیکم او كسوتهم او تحرير رقبة - ( آیت ۸۹ ،سورة المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اوسط کھانا کھلاؤ۔
(704) And it is permissible to give the fidyah for many prayers to one person in bulk, unlike the expiation of an oath. And Allah knows best. Translation: (704) Giving fidyah for many prayers to one poor person is permissible, contrary to the expiation of an oath [that giving all expiation to one poor person is not permissible]. Explanation: In fidyah, it is necessary to give half a sa' to a poor person; feeding is not necessary. Therefore, if one gives wheat for many fidyahs to one poor person, all fidyahs will be fulfilled. And in the expiation of an oath, feeding is the essence, and one may feed at most half a sa' to one miskin. So if one gives the food of several miskin to one, only the expiation of that one miskin will be fulfilled, not the others. Evidence: (1) In the fidyah of fasting, giving food is the essence; its proof is in the indication of this verse: 'And upon those who are able [to fast] is a fidyah of feeding a poor person' (2:184). This verse indicates to give wheat as fidyah. (2) And in the expiation of an oath, feeding is the essence, indicated by this verse: 'Allah will not take you to account for thoughtlessness in your oaths, but He will take you to account for your deliberate oaths; its expiation is to feed ten poor persons from the average of what you feed your families' (5:89). This verse instructs to feed average food.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This ruling discusses the permissibility of aggregating fidyah payments for missed prayers and giving them in lump sum to a single poor person. The key distinction is between fidyah and kaffarat yamin (expiation for a broken oath). For fidyah, the requirement is to give (give ownership of) half a sa' of wheat per missed act; feeding (consumption) is not required. Therefore, multiple fidyahs can be given to one faqir. For kaffarat yamin, the Quran requires 'it'am (feeding) of ten masakeen, and the Hanafi interpretation is that feeding involves actual consumption, so each miskin must be fed separately; giving the entire amount to one person does not fulfill the obligation for others. The proof for fidyah is Surah al-Baqarah 2:184, which says 'fidyatun ta'amu miskin' (feeding a poor person), but the Hanafi understanding is that giving ownership of the food suffices. For kaffarat yamin, Surah al-Ma'idah 5:89 specifies 'it'amu 'asharat masakin' (feed ten poor persons), implying distribution. Thus the distinction is maintained.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation for missed fasts/prayers, given as half a sa' of wheat per missed act.
کفارہ یمین (kaffarat yamin): Expiation for a broken oath, involving feeding ten poor persons or clothing them or freeing a slave.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, approximately 2.04 kg (or 1.75 kg wheat according to some). Here, half a sa' is given per fidyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to give fidyah for many prayers to a single poor person, but not for kaffarat yamin?
A) Because fidyah involves giving wheat, while kaffarat involves feeding.
B) Because the Quranic verse for fidyah does not specify distribution, while kaffarat explicitly requires ten poor persons.
C) Because fidyah is less serious.
D) Because the guardian prefers one person.

Key Takeaway
The legal nature of an obligation (financial vs. physical) determines distribution requirements.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Obligation of Order Between Missed and Present Prayers
Ruling with proof on tartib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib between missed and current prayers, explain the evidence from the Khandaq hadith, and identify the conditions under which order is wajib.

Core Idea
Order between missed and current prayers is wajib; the Prophet's delay of Maghrib proves its necessity.

This lesson examines a key ruling in the Hanafi school: when a person has missed a prayer (fa'itah) and the time for the current prayer has entered, must they pray the missed prayer first? The passage presents the ruling and its proofs, including the famous incident from the Battle of the Trench where the Prophet delayed Maghrib to make up 'Asr. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly performing qada' prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification is. Here, the act is 'observing order (tartib) between a missed prayer and the current prayer' and the ruling is that it is 'mustahaqq' (obligatory/deserved). In Hanafi terminology, this means it is wajib.
The passage also mentions order among multiple missed prayers, but we focus on the primary ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three proofs: a hadith from the Battle of Khandaq, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and a hadith from Ibn 'Umar (cut off). The main proof is the Khandaq hadith where the Prophet prayed the missed 'Asr before the current Maghrib.
The translation of the hadith is given in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the wajib status of order? The Prophet deliberately delayed Maghrib (which was on time) to pray 'Asr first. If order were not required, he would have prayed Maghrib on time and made up 'Asr later. His action indicates the necessity of order.
This is an example of al-amr (command) inferred from action.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and conditions
The Hanafi ruling is that order is wajib when the missed prayers are few (e.g., within a day) and one does not fear the current prayer's time will expire. If the current time is about to end, one should pray the current prayer first. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) also hold order as wajib but may differ on details.
The passage does not elaborate all conditions, but the commentary notes this.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a person deliberately reverses the order, the prayer is valid (sahih) but sinful (makruh tahrimi). This distinguishes the Hanafi position from any view that would invalidate the prayer.
This is derived from the general Hanafi principle that wajib omissions require compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but do not invalidate.

وجه : (۱) وقتیہ اور فوت شدہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔
ان عمر بن الخطاب جاء يوم الخندق بعد ما غربت الشمس فجعل يسب كفار قريش قال يا رسول الله ! ما صلى الله كدت اصلـى العصر حتى كادت الشمس تغرب قال النبي علم و الله ! ما صليتها ، فقمنا الى بطحان فتوضأ للصلاة وتوضأنا لها فصلى العصر بعد ما غربت الشمس ثم صلى بعدها المغرب . ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۸۷، الرجل یذکر صلوۃ علیہ وھو فی آخری ، ج اول ، ص۴۱۴، نمبر ۴۷۵۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ پہلے فائنہ نماز پڑھے اسکے بعد وقتیہ نماز پڑھے۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من
Chapter: Making Up Missed Prayers (Qada al-Fawa'it)
(705) The order between the missed prayer and the current time prayer, and between missed prayers among themselves, is obligatory (mustahaqq).
Chapter: On making up missed prayers
Essential note: Qada' al-fawa'it: Prayers that are lost and missed are called fawa'it. And performing them is called qada'. Making up prayers is fard. Because praying on time was fard; when one could not pray on time, now making up becomes fard. Its proof is this hadith: Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (Allah bless him and give him peace) said: Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that. And establish prayer for My remembrance (Ta-Ha 20:14). From this hadith and verse it is learned that praying missed prayer is fard.
Translation: (705) Order between missed and current time prayers, and between several missed prayers, is necessary.
Explanation: Here there are two issues: [1] One is that order between a missed prayer and a current time prayer is necessary: first pray the missed and then the current prayer. [2] The second issue is that if several prayers are missed, order among them is also necessary: for example, first pray Dhuhr, then 'Asr, then Maghrib, then 'Isha'.
Proof: (1) Order between current and missed is wajib; for this there is this hadith: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab came on the day of Khandaq after the sun had set, and he began cursing the disbelievers of Quraysh. He said: O Messenger of Allah! I almost did not pray 'Asr until the sun was about to set. The Prophet (Allah bless him and give him peace) said: By Allah, I did not pray it. So we went to Bathan, he performed wudu for prayer and we performed wudu, then he prayed 'Asr after the sun had set, and then after it he prayed Maghrib. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that the missed 'Asr was prayed first, then the current Maghrib. From this we learn that order between missed and current is necessary; otherwise, Maghrib would not have been delayed. (2) In this statement of a Tabi'i: From 'Amir and from Mughira from Ibrahim: They said: If you are in the 'Asr prayer and you remember that you did not pray Dhuhr, then break off and pray Dhuhr, then pray 'Asr. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) This athar indicates: pray the missed prayer first, then the current prayer. (3) Also in this hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah (Allah bless him and give him peace) said: Whoever...
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of order (tartib) when making up missed prayers (fawa'it). The matn (705) states: 'The order between the missed prayer and the current time prayer, and between missed prayers themselves, is mustahaqq (obligatory/deserved).' The commentary explains that this applies to two scenarios: (1) Between a single missed prayer and the current prayer: one must pray the missed prayer first if time remains for the current prayer; (2) Between multiple missed prayers: they must be prayed in their chronological order (e.g., Dhuhr before 'Asr, etc.). The proof is from three sources: a hadith from the Battle of Khandaq where the Prophet delayed Maghrib to first make up 'Asr, indicating the necessity of order; an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i saying one should break the current 'Asr to pray missed Dhuhr first; and another hadith from Ibn 'Umar (cut off here). The Hanafi ruling is that this order is wajib (obligatory) when the missed prayers are within the same day or few, and if the current prayer's time is not feared to pass. If one deliberately reverses, the prayer is valid but sinful (karahah tahrimiyyah). The note at the beginning also establishes that qada of any missed prayer is fard, based on the hadith and verse Ta-Ha 20:14.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tartib): Order of precedence, specifically praying missed prayers in their original chronological order and before the current prayer.
فوائت (fawa'it): Plural of fa'itah, missed prayers that are due to be made up.
فائتہ (fa'itah): A single missed prayer that needs to be made up.
مستحق (mustahaqq): Deserved, obligatory; in this context, it means the order is required (wajib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The hadith of the Battle of Khandaq where the Prophet prayed 'Asr after sunset before Maghrib
C) The statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i about breaking 'Asr to pray Dhuhr
D) The consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling is that order between a missed prayer and the current prayer is wajib, based on the Prophet's action of delaying Maghrib to make up 'Asr, and if violated the prayer is valid but sinful.

The Obligation of Making Up Missed Prayers
States ruling that qada of missed prayers is fard with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qada of missed prayers as fard and cite the primary evidence from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Making up a missed obligatory prayer is fard — the duty does not expire with time.

In this lesson, we examine one of the foundational rulings of salah: what happens when a fard prayer is missed? The Hanafi school holds that qada (making up) is fard based on clear textual evidence. We will dissect the proof and understand why this ruling is unanimous across schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qada of missed obligatory prayers. The ruling is fard (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik (Allah be pleased with him) and a Quranic verse (Surah Taha, 20:14).
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative verb 'falyusalli' (let him pray) indicates obligation according to Hanafi usul principles.
The verse 'Establish prayer for My remembrance' reinforces the importance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant difference among the schools on this ruling; it is muttafaq alayh.
All major madhhabs agree that qada of fard prayers is obligatory.
5
Understand the implication
The obligation to make up missed prayers is immediate upon remembrance, and no expiation (kaffarah) is required other than performing the prayer.

باب: نماز فوت شدہ کی قضا کے بیان میں ضروری نوٹ: قضاء الفوائت : جو نما ز فوت ہو جائے اور چھوٹ جائے اس کو فوائت کہتے ہیں ۔ اور اس کے پڑھنے کو قضا کہتے ہیں۔ نماز قضا کرنا فرض ہے۔ کیونکہ نماز کو وقت پر پڑھنا فرض تھا جب وقت پر نہ پڑھ سکا تو اب قضا کرنا فرض ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن انس بن مالک عن النبي الا الله قال من نسى صلوة فليصل اذا ذكر لا كفارة لها، الا ذلک واقم الصلوة لذكرى (آیت ۱۴ ، سورۃ طحه ۲۰) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من نسی صلوۃ فلیصل اذاذ کر، ص ۹۹، نمبر ۵۹۷ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی من نام عن صلوۃ اونسیها ،ص۷۰ نمبر ۴۳۵) اس حدیث اور آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ فوت نماز پڑھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter: On making up missed prayers. Necessary note: Qada' al-Fawa'it: Prayers that become missed and are left are called fawa'it. And reciting them is called qada'. Making up prayer is fard. Because praying on time was fard. When one could not pray on time, then making up becomes fard. Its proof is this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that.' And the verse: 'And establish prayer for My remembrance' (Surah Taha, 20:14). (Bukhari, chapter on whoever forgets prayer let him pray when he remembers, p. 99, no. 597; Abu Dawud, chapter on one who sleeps through prayer or forgets it, p. 70, no. 435). From this hadith and verse it is known that praying missed prayer is fard.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on missed prayers (qada' al-fawa'it) by establishing the fundamental ruling: making up missed prayers is obligatory (fard). The author first defines the key terms: missed prayers (fawa'it) and making them up (qada). He then explains the logic: since performing the prayer on time was fard, failing to do so does not remove the obligation; rather, the duty transforms into making it up. The proof is twofold: a hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded prayer upon remembrance, and the Qur'anic verse 'Establish prayer for My remembrance.' The hadith explicitly commands prayer when one remembers, indicating obligation. The verse underscores the connection between remembrance and prayer. This ruling is a principle accepted by all schools.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qaḍā' al-fawā'it): Making up missed obligatory prayers after their time has passed.
فوائت (fawā'it): Missed obligatory prayers that were not performed in their proper time.

The Obligation of Order (Tartīb) in Making Up Missed Prayers
Ruling on required order between missed and current prayers and among missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartīb and identify the evidence establishing its obligation.

Core Idea
When making up missed prayers, the missed prayer must be performed before the current one, and missed prayers must follow chronological order.

The Hanafi school holds that when a person has both a missed prayer and the current prayer to perform, order (tartīb) is obligatory. The same obligation applies when multiple prayers have been missed: they must be made up in their original sequence. In this passage, the author presents four proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions that establish tartīb as a legal requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two distinct obligations: (1) order between a missed prayer and the current prayer, and (2) order among multiple missed prayers. Note that both are labeled as 'wajib'.
The second ruling implies chronological order: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr.
2
Analyze the first proof (Hadith of Khandaq)
The hadith describes the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying the missed Asr after sunset before Maghrib. This deliberate delay of the current prayer (Maghrib) to perform the missed one indicates obligation.
This proof establishes the order between missed and current prayers.
3
Analyze the second proof (Saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i)
A Tabi'i states that if you are in Asr prayer and remember you missed Zuhr, you should leave and pray Zuhr first, then Asr. This shows the priority of the missed prayer over the current one.
It reinforces the first ruling with a direct instruction.
4
Analyze the third proof (Hadith on forgetting a prayer with imam)
The hadith instructs one who forgets a prayer and remembers while praying with an imam to complete the current prayer and then repeat the forgotten one, then repeat the current prayer to maintain order.
This implies that order is so important that the current prayer must be repeated after the missed one.
5
Analyze the fourth proof (Hadith on multiple missed prayers)
When the Prophet missed four prayers on the day of Khandaq, he prayed them in chronological order: Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha. This establishes the obligation of chronological order among missed prayers.
This proof directly addresses the second ruling.

ترجمه : (۷۰۵) نماز فوت شدہ اور وقتیہ اور چند فوت شدہ نمازوں کے مابین ترتیب ضروری ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں دو مسئلے ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ فوت شدہ نماز اور وقت یہ نماز کے درمیان ترتیب ضروری ہے۔ کہ پہلے فوت شدہ پڑھے اور اس کے بعد وقتیہ نماز پڑھے۔[۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر چند نماز فوت ہوئی ہو تو اس کے درمیان بھی ترتیب ضروری ہے ، مثلا پہلے ظہر کی نماز پڑھے، پھر عصر کی نماز پڑھے، پھر مغرب کی پھر عشاء کی نماز پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) وقتیہ اور فوت شدہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب جاء يوم الخندق بعد ما غربت الشمس فجعل يسب كفار قريش قال يا رسول الله ! ما صلى الله كدت اصلـى العصر حتى كادت الشمس تغرب قال النبي علم و الله ! ما صليتها ، فقمنا الى بطحان فتوضأ للصلاة وتوضأنا لها فصلى العصر بعد ما غربت الشمس ثم صلى بعدها المغرب . (بخارى شريف، باب من صلى بالناس جماعة بعد ذهاب الوقت ،ص ۹۹ نمبر ۵۹۶ / ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الرجل تفوته الصلوات بات تھن يبداً ،ص ۴۳، نمبر ۱۸۰/۱۷۹) اس حدیث میں عصر کی فائتہ پہلے پڑھی پھر مغرب کی وقتیہ پڑھی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فائنہ اور وقتیہ کے در میان ترتیب ضروری ہے۔ ورنہ تو مغرب کو مؤخر نہ کرتے ۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن عامر وعن مغيرة عن ابراهيم قالا : اذا كنت في صلوة العصر فذكرت أنك لم تصل الظهر فانصرف فصل الظهر ثم صل العصر . ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۸۷، الرجل یذکر صلوۃ علیہ وھو فی آخری ، ج اول ، ص۴۱۴، نمبر ۴۷۵۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ پہلے فائنہ نماز پڑھے اسکے بعد وقتیہ نماز پڑھے۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من نسى صلوة فلم يذكرها الا وهو مع الامام فليصل مع الامام فاذا فرغ من صلوته فليعد الصلوة التي نسى ثم للبيهة ليعد الصلوة التي صلى مع الامام ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب من ذکر صلوۃ و صوفی اخری ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۳ نمبر ۳۱۹۳ ردار قطنی ، باب الرجل يذكر صلوۃ وھو فی آخری ، ج اول ص ۴۰۰، نمبر ۱۵۴۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ بھی وقت یہ نماز پڑھی ہے تو فائتہ قضا کرے۔ ترتیب برقرار رکھنے کے لئے وقتیہ کو لوٹائے۔ (۴) اور فوت شدہ نماز کے درمیان میں ترتیب ضروری ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال عبد الله ان المشركين شغلوا رسول الله عن اربع صلوات يوم الخندق حتى ذهب من الليل ما شاء الله فامر بلالا فاذن ثم اقام فصلى الظهر ثم أقام فصلى العصر ثم أقام فصلى المغرب ثم أقام فصلى العشاء . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل تفوته الصلوات با تصن يبدأ ص ۲۳، نمبر ۱۷۹ رنسائی شریف ، باب کیف يقضی الفوائت من الصلوۃ ص ۸۵ نمبر ۶۲۳ ) اس حدیث میں ترتیب کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی گئی ہے۔ پہلے ظہر پھر عصر پھر مغرب پھر عشا پڑھی ہے۔
Translation: (705) Order between the missed prayer and the current prayer, and among missed prayers, is required. Explanation: There are two issues: [1] One is that order between missed prayer and current prayer is required: first perform the missed prayer, then the current prayer. [2] The second issue: if several prayers are missed, order is also required among them; e.g., first pray Zuhr, then Asr, then Maghrib, then Isha. Evidence: (1) For the obligation of order between current and missed: this hadith: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab came on the day of Khandaq after the sun had set, and began cursing the disbelievers of Quraysh...' (hadith continues). In this hadith, the missed Asr was prayed first, then the current Maghrib. This shows order is required, otherwise they would not have delayed Maghrib. (2) In this saying of a Tabi'i: '...if you are in Asr prayer and remember you did not pray Zuhr, then leave and pray Zuhr, then pray Asr.' (3) Also in this hadith: '...whoever forgets a prayer and only remembers while with the imam, let him pray with the imam, and when he finishes, let him repeat the prayer he forgot...' (4) And for order among missed prayers: this hadith: 'Abdullah said: The polytheists occupied the Prophet from four prayers on the day of Khandaq... so he ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah, and he prayed Zuhr, then Asr, then Maghrib, then Isha.' In this hadith, prayers were performed in order: Zuhr, then Asr, then Maghrib, then Isha.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on tartīb (order) when making up missed prayers. The author establishes two separate obligations: (1) when a person has both a missed prayer and the current prayer to perform, the missed prayer must be performed first before the current prayer; (2) when multiple prayers have been missed, they must be performed in their original chronological order (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr). Four proofs are adduced: the first is the well-known hadith of 'Umar on the day of Khandaq where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed the missed Asr after sunset before Maghrib. The second is the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a prominent Tabi'i, giving the same instruction. The third hadith about forgetting a prayer while with an imam implies order because the current prayer is repeated after the missed one. The fourth hadith directly shows the Prophet when he missed four prayers on the day of Khandaq, he prayed them in sequence. These proofs demonstrate that tartīb is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, not merely recommended.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The order prescribed in making up missed prayers: missed before current, and chronological order among missed.
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that was not performed in its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on order (tartīb) between a missed prayer and the current prayer?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Tartīb is wajib in the Hanafi school: missed prayers must be made up before current prayers and in chronological order.

Three Exceptions to the Obligatory Order in Missed Prayers
Lists three conditions that cancel the obligation of order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three conditions that drop the obligation of tartīb and apply them to determine the order of praying when multiple prayers are due.

Core Idea
Order between missed and current prayers drops when time is narrow, you forget, or you have six+ missed prayers (excluding witr).

You know that missed prayers must be made up in order before the current prayer. But what if you only have time for one? Or you simply forget? Or you have many missed prayers? The Hanafi school provides three clear exceptions where the strict order is relaxed, allowing you to pray the current prayer first. This lesson unpacks each condition and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Default Ruling
First, understand the base rule: it is wajib to pray missed prayers before the current prayer when there are few missed prayers, time permits, and one remembers.
Tartīb is an obligation in the Hanafi school; not all schools agree.
2
List the Three Exceptions
From the passage, extract the three situations that cancel this obligation: narrowness of the recommended time, forgetfulness during the current prayer, and having six or more missed prayers (excluding witr).
The text says 'by one of three things' – any one suffices.
3
Understand the Rationale for Each Exception
For narrow time: preserving the current prayer's time is primary. For forgetfulness: the hadith indicates that when one remembers, he prays the missed one, but if he remembers after finishing the current, order is dropped. For six prayers: numerous missed prayers make exact order burdensome.
The count excludes witr because it is not fard.
4
Apply the Exceptions
Given a scenario (e.g., only five minutes left for Zuhr, missed Fajr and Zuhr), determine whether tartīb is dropped and what order to follow.
If any condition is met, you may pray current first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۰۶) اور تین چیزوں سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے: ا مستحب وقت تنگ ہونے سے ،اصبح روایت میں۔ ...... بھول جائے۔ ... اور جب فوت شدہ نمازیں چھ ہو جائیں وتر کے سوا، اس لئے کہ ترتیب ساقط کرنے میں وتر کا شمار نہیں ہے، اگر چہ وتر میں ترتیب لازم ہے۔ تشریح : یہ تین باتیں ہوں تو فوت شدہ نماز اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہیں رہتی ۔ [1] مستحب وقت تنگ ہو گیا کہ اب اگر فوت شدہ نماز پڑھتے ہیں تو خود وقت والی نماز فوت ہو جائے گی ، ایسے وقت میں وقتیہ اور فوت شدہ نماز کے درمیان ترتیب نہیں رہے گی ، اب پہلے وقتیہ پڑھے، بعد میں فوت شدہ نماز پڑھے ۔[۲] وقت یہ نماز پڑھتے وقت یا د ہی نہیں رہا کہ مجھ پر فوت شدہ نماز باقی ہے۔[۳] فوت شدہ نماز چھ ہو جائیں تو اب ترتیب واجب نہیں رہی، اس لئے پہلے وقتیہ پڑھ سکتا ہے بعد میں فوت شدہ پڑھے ۔ یہ چھ نمازیں وقتیہ ہوں ، ان میں کوئی وتر نہ ہو۔ وجه : (۱) کیونکہ فوت شدہ نماز پڑھنے میں جب وقتیہ ہی قضاء ہو جائے گی تو فوت شدہ نماز کو کیسے پڑھیں؟ اس سے تو وقتیہ جو اصلی ہے اسکا حق مارا جائے گا۔ اسلئے وقت تنگ ہو تو ترتیب ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) بھول جائے تو فائنہ کا وقت نہیں رہا اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک عن النبي الله قال من نسى صلوة فليصل اذا ذكر لا كفارة لها، الا ذلک واقم الصلوة لذكرى (آیت ۱۴ ، سورۃ طحه ۲۰) ( بخاری شریف، باب من نسی صلوۃ فلیصل اذاذ کر ، ص ۱۹۹، نمبر
Translation: (706) And it is dropped by one of three things: narrowness of the recommended time (in the correct report), forgetfulness, and when the missed prayers become six besides witr, because witr is not counted in dropping order, although order is necessary in witr. Explanation: When these three things occur, the order between missed and current prayer is no longer obligatory. [1] The recommended time becomes narrow such that if one performs the missed prayer, the current prayer will be missed; in such a case, order does not remain; one should pray the current prayer first and then the missed prayer. [2] At the time of performing the current prayer, one does not remember that a missed prayer is outstanding. [3] When missed prayers become six, then order is no longer obligatory; therefore, one can pray the current prayer first and then the missed prayer. These six prayers are current ones, with no witr among them. Evidence: (1) Because if in performing the missed prayer, the current prayer will itself be missed, then how can one pray the missed prayer? That would violate the right of the current prayer which is primary. So when time is narrow, order is dropped. (2) If one forgets, the time for missed prayer has passed; for this there is this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that.' And the verse: 'Establish prayer for My remembrance.' (Surah Taha, 20:14) (Bukhari, p. 199, no.)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage lists the exceptions to the obligation of tartīb. The author identifies three situations that lift the requirement to pray missed prayers before the current prayer: (1) when the preferred time for the current prayer is so short that performing the missed prayer first would cause the current prayer to be missed entirely; (2) when one forgets that a missed prayer is outstanding at the time of the current prayer; (3) when the number of missed prayers reaches six or more, excluding witr. The rationale for the first is that the current prayer's time takes precedence, as it cannot be made up later without sin. For forgetfulness, the hadith 'whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers' implies that when he remembers, he prays the missed one immediately; but if he remembers only after finishing the current prayer, the order is dropped. The third is based on the principle that when missed prayers become numerous, maintaining exact order becomes overly burdensome, so the sharī'ah grants ease. Note that witr is excluded from the count of six because it is not a fard prayer, though order is still required for witr itself.

Key Terms
ضيق الوقت (ḍīq al-waqt): Narrowness of time such that performing the missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed.
النسيان (al-nisyān): Forgetting about the missed prayer during the current prayer; only if one has no recollection throughout the current prayer does tartīb drop.
ترتيب (tartīb): The obligation to pray missed prayers in the order they were missed before the current prayer.
وت (witr): The odd-numbered prayer prayed after the night prayer; it is emphasized sunnah or wajib (Hanafi). Excluded from the count of six because it is not fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many missed prayers (excluding witr) cause the order (tartīb) to be dropped according to the Hanafi school?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school drops the wajib of tartīb in three specific situations to prevent hardship: narrow time, forgetfulness, and six or more missed prayers (excluding witr).

Order Does Not Return When Missed Prayers Reduce Below Six
Ruling on permanence of dropping order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permanence of dropping order when missed prayers reduce below six and explain the threshold of kathrah.

Core Idea
Once order is dropped due to six or more missed prayers, it does not return even if the number drops below six.

This lesson addresses a key practical scenario: a person who has missed many prayers (six or more) loses the obligation to pray them in order. But what happens when they have made up some, reducing the count below six? The Hanafi school rules that the dropping of order is permanent. Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone making up missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person had seven missed prayers, triggering the dropping of order. They then prayed three, leaving four.
2
State the ruling
Order does not return even though the number is now fewer than six. The person does not become 'sahib tartib' again.
3
Understand the legal basis
The definition of kathrah (six or more) permanently alters the obligation. Once the threshold is crossed, the effect remains.
The relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يعد الترتيب بعودها الى القلّة ترجمه : (۷۰۷) اور کمی کی طرف لوٹنے کی وجہ سے ترتیب نہیں لوٹے گی۔ تشریح : مثلا سات نمازیں فوت ہوئی تھیں، جس کی وجہ سے ترتیب ختم ہو گئی تھی اب تین نمازیں پڑھ ڈالی اور چار نماز میں رہ گئیں تو اب یہ آدمی لوٹ کر صاحب ترتیب نہیں بنے گا، اور اس کے لئے فائنہ کو یاد کرتے ہوئے وقتیہ کو پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔ اصبح روایت ہیں ہے۔
And order does not return when they (the missed prayers) return to fewness. Translation: (707) And order does not return by returning to fewness. Explanation: For example, if seven prayers were missed, due to which order was dropped, and then three were prayed, leaving four, then this person does not become one with order again, and it is permissible for him to pray the current prayer while remembering the missed ones.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This is a ruling statement clarifying that the dropping of order due to many missed prayers (six or more) is permanent. Even if the number falls below six, order is not re-established. The example given: a person had seven missed prayers, so order is dropped. He then makes up three, leaving four. Despite being below six, he is not required to observe order for the remaining four. This means he can pray the current prayer before making up the missed four. The legal principle is that once the threshold for kathrah (multiplicity) is crossed, the effect remains even after reduction. This is the relied-upon position, as indicated by 'fi al-sahih' or 'al-sahih'. The authority weight is from the school's established rulings.

Key Terms
قلّة (qillah): Fewness; here meaning less than six missed prayers.
كثرة (kathrah): Multitude; six or more missed prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has missed 9 prayers and has made up 4, what is the ruling on order between the remaining 5 missed prayers and the current prayer?
A) Order must be observed.
B) Order is dropped, so he may pray the current prayer first.
C) Only if the current prayer is also missed.
D) Order returns after making up 4.

Key Takeaway
The dropping of order due to kathrah (six or more) is permanent; it does not revert when the count falls below six.

New Missed Prayer After Six Old Missed Prayers Does Not Restore Order
Ruling on effect of additional missed prayers on order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the effect of a new missed prayer on order when a person already has six missed prayers, and identify the correct narration (sahih riwayah) relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Once order is dropped due to six missed prayers, it remains dropped even if more prayers are missed.

This lesson addresses a specific nuance in the Hanafi ruling on order (tartib) in making up missed prayers. Once a person has missed six or more prayers, the obligation to observe chronological order is dropped. The question arises: if a new missed prayer occurs after those six, does the order return? The text clarifies that, according to the correct narration, it does not. This ruling prevents unnecessary hardship and simplifies the process of qada for those with many missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the baseline: six missed prayers cause order to drop
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person has less than six missed prayers, he must make them up in order (tartib). Once the number reaches six or more, order is no longer required. This is a concession to avoid excessive difficulty.
The threshold of six is a well-known Hanafi position.
2
Consider the additional missed prayer (the seventh)
After the six, if the person misses another prayer (e.g., the current prayer), does that new missed prayer re-impose the order? The text considers this scenario.
The new missed prayer is labeled 'jadd' (new) and the old ones 'qadim' (old).
3
Determine the ruling: does order return?
According to the correct narration (sahih riwayah), order does not return. The new missed prayer is simply added to the count, but the dropping of order is permanent.
There is an alternative view that order could return, but it is not relied upon.
4
Identify the correct narration and its authority
The text specifies 'sahih riwayah' (correct narration). This is the position of the authoritative transmitted texts (zahir al-riwayah) and is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
The alternative view is considered weak (marjuh).
5
Apply the principle to a real scenario
Think: A person has six missed Zuhr prayers. He then misses today's Zuhr. He does not need to pray today's missed prayer before the old ones; he can make them up in any order.
This ruling applies only when the six old ones were present before the new one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : ( ۷۰۸) اور نئی فوت ہو جائے چھ پرانی فوت ہونے کے بعد، تو صحیح روایت میں ترتیب نہیں لوٹے گی۔
Translation: (708) And if a new missed prayer occurs after six old missed prayers, then in the correct narration order does not return.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that addresses a nuance: if a person already has six missed prayers (so order is dropped), and then he misses another prayer (the seventh, but a 'new' one), the order does not return. In other words, the new missed prayer is added to the count, but since order was already dropped, it remains dropped. This means he is still not required to observe order between his missed prayers and the current prayer. This is the 'sahih riwayah' (correct narration) preferred by the author. The underlying principle is that once multiple prayers are missed (six), the dropping of order is permanent and not undone by additional missed prayers.

Key Terms
جَدّ (jadd): New (occur), here meaning a new missed prayer subsequent to the existing six.
قدیم (qadim): Previous/old, referring to the first set of missed prayers that caused order to drop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct narration in this text, if a person has six missed prayers (so order is dropped), and then he misses another prayer, what is the ruling on order?
A) Order is restored because the new missed prayer counts as a fresh start
B) Order remains dropped
C) Order becomes wajib for the new missed prayer only
D) He must make up the new missed prayer first

Key Takeaway
Once order is dropped due to six missed prayers, it stays dropped even if more prayers are missed; this is the correct narration in the Hanafi school.

Six Missed Prayers Drop the Order (Tarteeb) in Qada
Establishes the threshold of six missed prayers for dropping tarteeb and rules on its return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when the obligation of tarteeb (order) in making up missed prayers is dropped, and explain why it does not return.

Core Idea
Six missed prayers (excluding witr) drop the obligation of order, and once dropped, order never returns.

Making up missed prayers (qada al-fawa'it) is an essential act of worship, but how do we prioritise? In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi threshold for dropping the requirement of chronological order (tarteeb) based on authentic narrations and the practice of the salaf. You will learn the key conditions that excuse a person from observing order and the critical principle that once the order is dropped, it is permanently lifted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and its droppers
Start by noting that tarteeb is wajib in making up missed prayers. Then list the three conditions that drop it: (1) forgetting, (2) fear of missing the current timely prayer, (3) having six or more missed prayers (excluding witr).
Witr is excluded from counting toward the six.
2
Examine the proofs for dropping tarteeb
The text cites a hadith (pray when you remember) and athar from al-Hasan, Ibrahim, and Ibn Umar. For forgetting and fear, the proof is the hadith and the athar of al-Hasan. For the six threshold, the athar of Ibrahim on fainting and Ibn Umar's practice are used.
These proofs are from the Salaf (tabi'un) not directly from the Prophet, but they are considered authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the non-return of tarteeb
The passage emphatically states that once tarteeb is dropped (e.g., by having six missed prayers), it does not return even if the number later reduces (e.g., from seven to four) or if a new missed prayer occurs after making up all old ones.
The 'asahh riwayah' (soundest narration) is that tarteeb is permanently lost.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who missed seven prayers, then prayed three. He still has four missed. He may pray the current timely prayer before making up the four because tarteeb is dropped. Later, if he makes up all seven, tarteeb does not return.
This is the mufta bihi position.

باب قضاء الفوائت
الفوائت ستّا غير الوتر فانه لا يعدّ مُسقِطا وان لزم ترتيبه . (۷۰) ولم يعد الترتيب بعودها الى القلّة ۱/۵۹۷ بود او دشریف، باب فی من نام عن صلوۃ اوسیھا، ص۷۰، نمبر ۴۳۵) اس حدیث اور آیت میں فلیصلی اذاذکر، سے معلوم ہوا کہ یاد آئے تب اس کا وقت ہوتا ہے۔ (۳) اور بھول جائے تو ترتیب ساقط ہوگی اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے . عن الحسن قال : اذا نسى الصلوات فليبدأ بالاولى فالاولى فان خاف الفوت يبدأ بالتي يخاف فوتها . (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ، باب ۲۸۳ فی الرجل ینسی الصلوات جمیعا ، ج اول ص ۴۱۰، نمبر ۴۷۲۵) اس اثر میں دونوں باتیں ہیں ، بھول جائے تب بھی ترتیب ساقط ہوگی، اور وقتیہ فوت ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تب بھی ترتیب ساقط ہوگی ۔ (۴) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ سالت الحكم و حماد ا عن رجل ذكر صلوة و هو في صلوة قالا : اذا ذكرها قبل أن يتشهد أو يجلس مقدار التشهد ترک هذه و عاد الى تلك فان ذکرها بعد ذالک اعتد بهذه و عاد الى تلک . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۲۸۷ الرجل یذکر صلوۃ علیہ وھو فی آخری، ج اول، ص ۴۱۴، نمبر ۶۱ ۴۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بھول کر عصر کی نماز پوری پڑھ لی بعد میں یاد آیا کہ مجھ پر ظہر کی نماز قضاء ہے تو اب ترتیب ساقط ہوگئی اور عصر کی نماز صحیح ہوگئی ۔ (۵) اور چھ نماز سے زیادہ ہو جائے تو وہ کثیر ہے جس سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عـن ابــراهيـم قـال : كان يقول في المغمى عليه اذا أغمى لمف عليه يوم وليلة أعاد و اذا كان اكثر من ذالك لم يعد - (مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ، ۵۴۷ ما يعيد النغمى عليه من الصلوة ، ج ، مایعید می ثانی ص اے نمبر ۶۵۹ /مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صلوۃ المریض على الدابة وصلوۃ اعمی علیہ، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۱۷، نمبر ۴۱۶۳) (۱) عن نافع عن ابن عمر أنه أغمى عليه أياما فأعاد صلوة يومه الذى أفاق فيه و لم يعد شيئا مما مضى . (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۵۴۷ ما یعید اعظمی علیه من الصلوۃ ، ج ثانی، ص ،اے نمبر ۶۵۸۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب صلوة المريض على الدابة وصلوة المغمی علیہ، ج ثانی ص ۳۱۷ نمبر ۴۱۶۳) ان دونوں اثروں سے معلوم ہوا کہ چھٹی نماز قضاء ہوجائے تب وہ کثیر ہوگی ۔ لغت : واذا صارت الفوائت ستا غیر الوتر فانہ لابعد مسقطا: اس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وتر اور وقتی نماز میں ترتیب واجب ہے ، چنانچہ وتر قضا ہو جائے ، اور یاد ہو اور وقت میں گنجائش ہو تو فجر سے پہلے پڑھنا ضروری ہے۔ لیکن خود وتر ترتیب ساقط کرنے کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے، چناچہ پانچ وقت یہ نماز فوت ہوئی ہو اور چھٹی و تر ہو تو بھی ترتیب ساقط نہیں ہوگی ، کیونکہ چھٹی نماز وقتیہ نہیں ہے وتر ہے ترجمه : (۷۰۷) اور کمی کی طرف لوٹنے کی وجہ سے ترتیب نہیں لوٹے گی۔ تشریح : مثلا سات نمازیں فوت ہوئی تھیں، جس کی وجہ سے ترتیب ختم ہو گئی تھی اب تین نمازیں پڑھ ڈالی اور چار نماز میں رہ گئیں تو اب یہ آدمی لوٹ کر صاحب ترتیب نہیں بنے گا، اور اس کے لئے فائنہ کو یاد کرتے ہوئے وقتیہ کو پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔ اصبح روایت
ہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : ( ۷۰۸) اور نئی فوت ہو جائے چھ پرانی فوت ہونے کے بعد، تو صحیح روایت میں ترتیب نہیں لوٹے گی۔
تشریح : مثلا تین مہینے پہلے چھ نمازیں فوت ہوئی تھیں، جس کی وجہ سے وہ صاحب ترتیب نہیں رہا تھا، پھر ان سب کو ادا کر چکا تھا، اب آج پھر ایک نماز فوت ہوگئی تو یہ اب صاحب ترتیب نہیں ہے اس لئے فائنہ کو یاد کرتے ہوئے وقتہ نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اصبح روایت یہی ہے۔ اصول : ایک مرتبہ صاحب ترتیب ختم ہونے کے بعد سب نمازیں قضا کرنے سے بھی صاحب ترتیب نہیں بنے گا۔
Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers. The missed prayers are six excluding witr, for it is not counted as dropping [tarteeb] even though its order is obligatory. (70) And tarteeb does not return by their reduction to few. (Hadith reference) From this hadith and verse 'fasalli li dhikri' it is understood that when he remembers, that is its time. (3) And if he forgets, tarteeb is dropped; for this is the saying of a tabi'i: from al-Hasan who said: When one forgets prayers, he should begin with the first then the next; if he fears missing [the current prayer], he begins with what he fears missing. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, No. 4725). In this athar there are both matters: when he forgets, tarteeb is dropped, and when there is fear of missing the timely prayer, tarteeb is also dropped. (4) There is also in this saying of a tabi'i: I asked al-Hakam and Hammad about a man who remembered a prayer while in another prayer; they said: If he remembers before tashahhud or sitting the amount of tashahhud, he leaves this and returns to that; if he remembers after that, he completes this and returns to that. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, No. 6147). In this athar it is that someone forgot and prayed Asr completely, then later remembered that he owed Dhuhr, then tarteeb was dropped and the Asr prayer became valid. (5) And if it becomes more than six prayers, then it is many (kathir) which drops tarteeb; for this is the saying of a tabi'i: from Ibrahim who said: He used to say about the one who fainted: if he faints for a day and a night, he repeats; if more than that, he does not repeat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, No. 6585/ Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, No. 4163). (1) From Nafi' from Ibn Umar that he fainted for days, so he repeated the prayer of the day he regained consciousness and did not repeat anything of what had passed. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, No. 6585/ Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, No. 4163). From these two athars it is understood that when the sixth missed prayer occurs, it becomes kathir. Lexical: 'When the missed prayers become six excluding witr, then it is not counted as dropping': The meaning of this phrase is that tarteeb is obligatory in witr and timely prayers, so if witr is missed and he remembers and there is scope in time, it is necessary to pray it before Fajr. But witr itself is not sufficient for dropping tarteeb, so if five timely prayers are missed and the sixth is witr, tarteeb is not dropped because the sixth is not a timely prayer, it is witr. Translation (707): And tarteeb does not return by their reduction to few. Explanation: For example, seven prayers were missed, so tarteeb was dropped; then he prayed three and four remained; then this person does not become a person of tarteeb, and for him it is permissible to pray the timely prayer while remembering the missed one. The soundest narration is this. Translation (708): And nor by a new missed prayer after six old ones, according to the soundest narration. Explanation: For example, three months ago six prayers were missed, so he was not a person of tarteeb; then he made them all up; then today another prayer is missed; so now he is not a person of tarteeb, therefore it is permissible to pray the timely prayer while remembering the missed one. The soundest narration is this. Principle: Once the status of having tarteeb is lost, even making up all prayers does not restore it.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Hanafi ruling on tarteeb (order) in making up missed prayers (qada al-fawa'it). The author establishes that six missed prayers (excluding witr) constitute 'kathir' (many) and drop the requirement of order. The proofs include hadith (the command to pray upon remembering) and athar from tabi'in (Hasan, Ibrahim, etc.) showing that forgetting, fear of missing the current prayer, or having six or more missed prayers all lift the order. Once tarteeb is dropped, it does not return even if the number of missed prayers later reduces below six (e.g., from seven to four), and a new missed prayer after a prior six also does not restore tarteeb. The key principle is that once a person ceases to be 'sahib tarteeb', making up all missed prayers does not revive the order. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah as indicated by 'asahh riwayah' (soundest narration) and 'usul' (principle).

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that need to be made up (qada).
ترتیب (tarteeb): The required order in making up missed prayers: one should pray missed prayers in their chronological order before the current timeliness prayer if possible.
مسقط (musqit): Something that drops the obligation of tarteeb; the six missed prayers (excluding witr) are a musqit.
کثیر (kathir): Many (missed prayers): six or more excluding witr, which drops tarteeb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT drop the obligation of tarteeb?
A) Forgetting a missed prayer while performing another prayer.
B) Fearing the current prayer's time will end.
C) Missing six Fajr prayers (excluding witr).
D) Missing three Zuhr prayers and three Asr prayers (total six, excluding witr).

Key Takeaway
Six missed fard prayers (excluding witr) permanently drop the obligation of order (tarteeb) in making up prayers; once dropped, it never returns.

Salah — Prayer

Suspended Invalidity: Praying a Current Fard While Remembering a Missed Prayer
Explains the suspended invalidity of current fard when remembering a missed prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling of suspended invalidity (fasad mawquf) to scenarios involving a person with less than six missed prayers and determine when prayers become nafl or revert to fard.

Core Idea
A current fard prayed while remembering a missed one is suspended — valid if five more are prayed, otherwise becomes nafl.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced rule from the Hanafi school about the obligation of order (tarteeb) in making up missed prayers. When a person is still bound by order (less than six missed), praying a timely fard before making up the missed one triggers suspended invalidity. The outcome depends on whether the total number of prayers reaches six, which drops the order obligation and validates the earlier prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory order (tarteeb)
Establish that the person is a 'sahib tarteeb' — they have missed fewer than six fard prayers. In this state, they must make up missed prayers in order before praying timely ones.
The threshold is six prayers; witr is excluded.
2
Recognize the suspended invalidity
If a person prays a current fard while remembering a missed one (and tarteeb is still wajib), the current prayer becomes invalid in a suspended manner — it is not immediately valid nor invalid permanently.
The term 'fasad mawquf' indicates the ruling is conditional.
3
Trace the two possible outcomes
If the person prays five timely prayers after the missed one (so total inclusive of the missed becomes six), the condition (tarteeb) drops and all five prayers become valid fard. If the missed prayer is made up before completing five timely prayers, the earlier prayers become nafl and must be repeated as fard.
The key is the total count reaching six, not the order of qada.
4
Apply the principle to examples
Work through scenarios: e.g., one missed + four timely prayed = nafl; then a fifth timely before qada makes total six → those four revert to fard. If qada done before fifth timely, they remain nafl.
The principle: once tarteeb is dropped (by six), it does not return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الخامسة بطل تشریح : مثلا تین مہینے پہلے چھ نمازیں فوت ہوئی تھیں، جس کی وجہ سے وہ صاحب ترتیب نہیں رہا تھا، پھر ان سب کو ادا کر چکا تھا، اب آج پھر ایک نماز فوت ہوگئی تو یہ اب صاحب ترتیب نہیں ہے اس لئے فائنہ کو یاد کرتے ہوئے وقتہ نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اصبح روایت یہی ہے۔ اصول : ایک مرتبہ صاحب ترتیب ختم ہونے کے بعد سب نمازیں قضا کرنے سے بھی صاحب ترتیب نہیں بنے گا۔ ترجمه : (۷۰۹) پس اگر فرض نماز فاستہ کو یاد کرتے ہوئے پڑھی، چاہے وتر ہی کیوں نہ ہو تو اس کی نماز موقوف طور پر فاسد ہوگی۔، پھر اگر اس چھوڑی ہوئی نماز کو یادر کھتے ہوئے اس کے بعد پانچ نمازیں پڑھ لیں تو سب صحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر بعد میں چھوٹی ہوئی نماز کو قضا کرنے سے نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اگر چھ نماز قضا ہو گئیں تو ترتیب ختم ہو جائے گی، اور اس کے لئے وقت یہ پڑھنا جائز ہوگا ، اور چھ سے کم ہیں تو چھ نمازیں قضا ہونے تک وقتیہ نماز باطل ہوتی جائیں گیں اور نفل بنتی جائیں گیں ۔ پھر چھٹی نماز باطل ہوئی تو سب پلٹ کر فرض بن جائیں گیں۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمثلا ایک نماز فوت ہوئی ، اب اس کو یاد کرتے ہوئے چار نمازیں پڑھ لیں ، تو چاروں نمازیں نفل بن جائیں گئیں، کیونکہ یہ ابھی تک صاحب ترتیب ہے اور اس نے ترتیب کے خلاف کیا، لیکن ابھی پہلی نماز ادا نہیں کی کہ پانچویں نماز پڑھ لی تو سب ملا کر چھ نماز میں ہو گئیں، اس لئے ترتیب ختم ہوگئی ، اس لئے وہ پانچ نمازیں جو باطل ہو کر نفل بنی تھیں وہ سب لوٹ کر فرض بن جائیں گیں ۔ اور اگر پانچویں نماز پڑھنے سے پہلے پہلی فوت شدہ نماز ادا کر لی تو یہ جو چار نمازیں پڑھیں تھیں وہ فل ہی باقی رہیں گیں ، کیونکہ یہ ابھی صاحب ترتیب ہے، اس لئے ان نمازوں کو دوبارہ فرض کے طور پڑھنی ہوگی۔ ترجمه : (۷۱۰) اگر پانچوں نماز کے وقت کے نکل جانے سے پہلے اس فوت شدہ نماز کی قضا کرے گا تو اس فوت شدہ کے یاد رکھتے ہوئے اس کی قضا کرنے سے پہلے جو نمازیں پڑھی ہوں اس کی فرضیت باطل ہو کر صرف نفل ہو جائے گی ۔ تشریح : پانچویں نماز کے پڑھنے سے پہلے پہلی فوت شدہ نماز پڑھ لی تو یہ صاحب ترتیب باقی رہا کیونکہ مجموعہ نمازیں چھ نہیں ہوئیں ، اس لئے اس کی پہلی چار نماز میں جو فرض پڑھی تھیں وہ فضل میں تبدیل ہو گئیں، اس لئے ان چاروں نمازوں کو دوبارہ فرض کے طور پر پڑھنی چاہئے۔
Translation (709): So if one prays a fard while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, his prayer becomes invalid in a suspended way. Then if the time of the fifth prayer of those he prayed after the missed one while remembering it expires, all become valid, and they are not invalidated by making up the missed one afterwards. (10) And if he makes up the missed prayer before the time of the fifth expires, [the previous prayers] become invalid. Explanation: For example, three months ago six prayers were missed, so he was not a person of tarteeb; then he made them all up; then today another prayer is missed; so now he is not a person of tarteeb, therefore it is permissible to pray the timely prayer while remembering the missed one. The soundest narration is this. Principle: Once the status of having tarteeb is lost, even making up all prayers does not restore it. Translation (709): So if one prays a fard while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, his prayer becomes invalid in a suspended way. Then if he prays five prayers after that missed one while remembering it, all become valid. Then making up the missed prayer afterwards does not invalidate them. Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that if six prayers are missed, tarteeb is dropped, and for him it is permissible to pray the timely one. If less than six, then until six are missed, the timely prayers become invalid and become nafl. Then when the sixth is invalidated, they all revert to fard. The scenario: For example, one prayer is missed; then he prays four prayers while remembering it; these four become nafl because he is still a person of tarteeb and acted against order. But before he makes up the first missed prayer, he prays the fifth prayer, so total becomes six; thus tarteeb is dropped, and those five prayers that were invalid and became nafl all revert to fard. But if he makes up the first missed prayer before praying the fifth, then those four prayers remain nafl, because he is still a person of tarteeb, so he must repeat them as fard. Translation (710): If he makes up the missed prayer before the time of the five prayers expires, then the fard obligation of those prayers prayed before the qada becomes invalid and they become merely nafl. Explanation: If he prays the first missed prayer before praying the fifth prayer, he remains a person of tarteeb because the total number of prayers has not reached six. Therefore the first four prayers he prayed as fard are converted to nafl, so he must repeat those four as fard.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi ruling on a person who prays a current fard prayer while remembering a previously missed prayer (faa'itah). The key principle is tarteeb: if one is still bound by order (i.e., has missed less than six prayers), praying a current prayer before making up the missed one invalidates the current prayer in a suspended way. The invalidation is 'suspended' (mawquf): if the person later makes up the missed prayer after having prayed five timely prayers (the missed one plus four more), then all five become valid because the number reaches six, dropping tarteeb. However, if he makes up the missed prayer before completing the fifth timely prayer (i.e., before six total), then the current prayers remain invalid (they become nafl) and must be repeated as fard. The commentary emphasizes that the threshold of six is crucial. The ruling builds on the previous lesson: once tarteeb is dropped (by six or more missed prayers), it does not return; here, the opposite case is shown—when the person is still bound by order (less than six missed), praying out of order causes suspended invalidity until the threshold is crossed.

Key Terms
فساد موقوف (fasad mawquf): Suspended invalidity: a prayer is initially invalid but becomes valid upon fulfillment of a condition (here, the completion of five prayers after the missed one).
صاحب ترتیب (sahib tarteeb): A person who is bound to maintain order in making up missed prayers, i.e., has less than six missed prayers (excluding witr).
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; here, a fard prayer that becomes nafl due to violation of tarteeb, requiring repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone misses one fard prayer and then prays four timely fard prayers while remembering the missed one, and then makes up the missed prayer before praying the fifth timely prayer, what is the status of those four timely prayers?
A) They become valid fard because the missed one is made up
B) They become nafl and must be repeated as fard
C) They remain fard because tarteeb is not required
D) They are invalid and must be repeated as qada

Key Takeaway
The ruling on suspended invalidity hinges on the threshold of six missed prayers: below six, order is wajib and prayers are suspended; at six, order drops and prayers become valid.

The Ruling on Missed Prayer After Completing Six
States the correct opinion on the validity of a recent missed prayer after completing six old ones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a recent missed prayer reinstates the obligation of order after completing six missed prayers.

Core Idea
Completing six missed prayers does not restore the obligation of order; the status of ṣāḥib tartīb is permanently dropped.

In the chapter on making up missed prayers, the author presents the correct Hanafi opinion concerning a person who has missed six prayers, made them up, and then misses another prayer. The ruling clarifies that the recent missed prayer does not invalidate the previously dropped order. This lesson will help you grasp this key exception in the rules of tartīb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage asks whether a recent missed prayer (after making up six old ones) reinstates the obligation to pray in order (tartīb).
The term 'ḥadīthah' (recent) refers to the latest missed prayer.
2
State the Hanafi position
The correct opinion (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that the recent missed prayer does not invalidate; the person remains not obligated to observe order.
The phrase 'alā al-aṣaḥḥ fīhimā' indicates the preferred view in both matters (the six old ones and the recent one).
3
Understand the concept of ṣāḥib tartīb
A person becomes ṣāḥib tartīb only when the missed prayers are fewer than six. Missing six or more permanently removes this status, even after making them up.
The status does not return after qaḍā'.
4
Memorize the ruling
Commit to memory: 'ولا بفوت حديثه بعد ست قديمةٍ على الاصح فيهما' — the recent missed prayer does not cause invalidity after six old ones, on the correct opinion.
This phrase is a key memorization anchor for the chapter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت (۷۰۸) ولا بفوت حديثه بعد ست قديمةٍ على الاصح فيهما
Chapter of Making up Missed Prayers (708) And it is not invalidated by its being recent after six old ones, on the correct opinion concerning both.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the order (tartīb) of prayers. The author, following the preferred narration (al-aṣaḥḥ), states that if a person missed six prayers previously, completed them, and then missed another prayer, that later missed prayer does not invalidate the order. The Urdu commentary explains that once a person misses six prayers, they lose the status of ṣāḥib tartīb (one obligated to pray in order). Even after making up those six, this status is not regained. Therefore, it is permissible to pray the current prayer while remembering the missed one.

Key Terms
فوت (fawt): Missing or losing a prayer; the state of having missed a prayer.
صاحب ترتیب (ṣāḥib tartīb): One who is obligated to pray in sequence, i.e., cannot pray a current prayer before making up a missed one.
ترتیب (tartīb): Order; the obligation to make up missed prayers in sequence before performing current prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The person is still obligated to pray in order.
B) The later missed prayer does not invalidate the order; the person is no longer ṣāḥib tartīb.
C) The person must make up the later missed prayer before any current prayer.
D) The person must repeat all six prayers again.

Key Takeaway
Once a person misses six prayers, the obligation to pray in order (tartīb) is permanently dropped, and making them up does not reinstate it.

Suspended Invalidity of a Fard Prayed While Remembering a Missed Prayer
Explains suspended invalidity of a fard prayed while remembering a missed prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of fasād mawqūf, identify the conditions that trigger it, and apply the rule of ṣāḥib tartīb to determine whether a prayer becomes valid or becomes nāfil.

Core Idea
A fard prayed out of order while ṣāḥib tartīb is suspended until five prayers pass.

You are about to explore a unique Hanafi ruling on prayer order (tartīb). When a person who still owes fewer than six missed prayers (ṣāḥib tartīb) prays a current fard while remembering a missed one, that prayer is not immediately invalid—it enters a state of suspension. Its final status depends on whether the total number of missed prayers reached six. This lesson will help you parse the reasoning behind this suspended invalidity and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The passage states that if someone prays a fard while remembering a missed fard (including witr as fard), that prayer becomes invalid with 'suspended invalidity' (fasād mawqūf). Note the key term: the invalidity is not immediate but conditional.
The Arabic uses 'فسادا موقوفا' - a technical term meaning pending determination.
2
Understand the condition that lifts the suspension
If the time of the fifth prayer (after the missed one) passes, and all these prayers were performed while still remembering the missed prayer, they all become valid. This is because the missed prayer plus these five make six, and with six missed prayers the obligation of order (tartīb) drops.
The threshold is six total missed prayers; order is only required for five or fewer.
3
Consider the intermediate scenario
What if only four prayers are prayed after the missed one? Since the person remains ṣāḥib tartīb (fewer than six missed), those four prayers become nāfil (supererogatory) because they violated order. They must be repeated as fard after making up the missed prayer.
This is derived from the commentary; the text explicitly mentions only the result after five prayers.
4
Apply the concept of ṣāḥib tartīb
The person is ṣāḥib tartīb if the number of missed prayers is five or fewer. When the total reaches six (the missed prayer plus five prayed out of order), the obligation of order ceases, and the prayers become valid as fard.
Ṣāḥib tartīb is defined by having less than six missed prayers.
5
Distinguish between suspended invalidity and absolute invalidity
Suspended invalidity means the prayer is neither valid nor invalid immediately. Its status depends on a future condition (whether the order obligation drops). Absolute invalidity would require immediate repetition. This distinction is crucial for understanding the ruling.
Misunderstanding this leads to incorrect repetition of valid prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۰۹) فلو صلى فرضا ذاكرا فائتة ولو وترا فسد فرض رضه فساد اموقوفا فان خرج وقت الخامسة مما صلاه بعد المتروكة ذاكرا لها صحت جميعها فلا تبسط بقضاء المتروكة بعده
(709) If he prays a fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, then his prayer becomes invalid with suspended invalidity. If the time of the fifth prayer passes, from what he prayed after the missed one while remembering it, all become valid. Then making up the missed one afterward does not invalidate them.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling on the effect of remembering a missed prayer while performing a current prayer. The author explains that if a person who is still ṣāḥib tartīb (obligated to pray in order) prays a fard while remembering a missed fard, that current prayer becomes suspended (mawqūf). It is neither fully valid nor fully invalid at that moment. If the person then prays four more prayers while still remembering the same missed prayer (making a total of five prayers after the missed one), and the time of the fifth prayer passes, then all these five prayers become valid. This is because the missed prayer, together with these five, makes six, which removes the obligation of order. Then even if the missed prayer is made up later, the previously prayed prayers remain valid. The Urdu commentary elaborates with examples: if one missed one prayer and then prayed four while remembering it, those four become nāfil (supererogatory) because he was still ṣāḥib tartīb. But if he then prays a fifth (making five after the missed one), then the total missed and prayed becomes six, so the order obligation drops, and those four turn back into fard.

Key Terms
فساد موقوف (fasād mawqūf): Suspended invalidity; a prayer that is neither valid nor invalid until a later condition determines its status.
صاحب ترتیب (ṣāḥib tartīb): One who is obligated to pray in sequence due to having less than six missed prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a fard prayer prayed while remembering a missed prayer, if the person later prays exactly five more fard prayers (all while remembering the same missed prayer) and the time of the fifth prayer passes?
A) All five prayers are invalid and must be repeated.
B) All five prayers become valid as fard.
C) The first four prayers become nāfil and the fifth is fard.
D) All five prayers become nāfil.

Key Takeaway
A fard prayed out of order while ṣāḥib tartīb is suspended; it becomes fard if five more are prayed, otherwise it becomes nāfil.

Making Up the Missed Prayer Before the Fifth: Effect on Earlier Prayers
Expands on the ruling for ṣāḥib tartīb when the missed prayer is made up early.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a ṣāḥib tartīb makes up a missed fard prayer before the expiry of the fifth prayer and explain the consequence for the prayers offered in the meantime.

Core Idea
Making up a missed fard before the fifth prayer's time ends transforms earlier prayers into nāfil, requiring re-offering as fard.

In a previous lesson, we learned that a person who has missed a fard prayer (ṣāḥib tartīb) must pray the missed one before the current ones. If he prays out of order, the out-of-order prayers become nāfil—but only if the missed prayer is eventually made up before the time of the fifth prayer expires. This lesson expands on that condition and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Recall the scenario
Remember the ṣāḥib tartīb scenario: a person misses one fard (e.g., Fajr) and remembers it while praying other fard prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha) in order. The missed prayer remains undone.
This is the base case from the previous ruling.
2
Identify the timing of the make‑up
The person makes up the missed prayer before the time of the fifth prayer (the next day's Fajr) expires. This is the critical condition—if he makes it up after that time, or if the total missed prayers reach six, the obligation of tartīb drops entirely.
The 'fifth prayer' refers to the one that would come after the four prayed out of order (e.g., the next Fajr if the four were Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha).
3
Apply the rule for out‑of‑order prayers
Since the missed prayer is made up before the deadline, the obligation of tartīb remains. Therefore, the four prayers that were offered before the make‑up were not in correct sequence. Hanafi fiqh rules that such prayers become valid only as nāfil (supererogatory), not as fard.
This is because fard performance requires correct order (tartīb) according to the Hanafi school.
4
State the consequence
The four prayers become nāfil. The person has not fulfilled his fard obligation for those four. Therefore, he must re‑offer each of them as fard (i.e., repeat Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha with proper intention).
No penalty or sajdah sahw is needed; the prayers themselves are valid as nāfil, but the fard duty remains unfulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصف ما صلاه متذكرا قبلها وصار نفلا
And a description of what he prayed while remembering before it, and it became nāfil.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This short Arabic phrase likely continues the previous ruling. The Urdu commentary explains that if before the time of the fifth prayer expires, the person makes up the missed prayer (while still remembering it), then the prayers that were prayed earlier (while remembering the missed one) become nāfil permanently. Since the total missed prayers did not reach six (because the missed one was made up before the fifth), the obligation of order remains, so the out-of-order prayers become nāfil and must be re-offered as fard.

Key Terms
صاحب ترتيب (ṣāḥib tartīb): A person who has missed a fard prayer and remembers it, thus being obligated to pray the missed one before the current ones.
نفل (nāfil): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer; not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a ṣāḥib tartīb makes up the missed fard prayer before the time of the fifth prayer expires, what is the status of the prayers he offered while remembering the missed one?
A) They become valid fard.
B) They become nāfil and must be repeated as fard.
C) They become bātil and must be completely repeated.
D) They become nāfil and need not be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Making up a missed fard before the fifth prayer's time causes earlier out-of-order prayers to become nāfil; they must be repeated as fard.

Specifying Missed Prayers: The Facilitation of First or Last
Provides a facilitation for specifying numerous missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'yīn for multiple missed prayers and apply the facilitation of intending the first or last.

Core Idea
Many missed prayers require specification; but intending first or last suffices for ease.

When a person has missed many prayers of the same type, such as several Zuhr prayers, it is necessary to specify which particular prayer is being made up. However, to alleviate difficulty, the Hanafi school allows a simplified intention: one may intend the first or the last of those missed prayers. This ruling balances legal precision with practical mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
The text states that when missed prayers (fawā'it) are many, specification (ta'yīn) of each prayer is required. Understand that without specification, the qaḍā' may not be valid.
The term 'ta'yīn' means identifying the specific prayer by its type and time.
2
Recognize the facilitation
If one wishes to make the matter easy, he may intend the first Zuhr that is due upon him or the last. This is a concession (rukhsah) to avoid undue hardship.
The facilitation applies only when the same type of prayer is missed multiple times (e.g., several Zuhrs).
3
Apply to a scenario
For example, if a person missed five Zuhr prayers over several days, he can make them up by intending each specific day, or for ease, he can intend 'the first Zuhr upon me' or 'the last Zuhr upon me' for each prayer he performs.
The intention must be made at the beginning of the prayer. The facilitation does not remove the need to pray each missed prayer; it only simplifies the intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۱۱) واذا كثرت الفوائت يحتاج لتعيين كل صلوة فان اراد تسهيل الامر علیه نوی اول ظهر عليه و آخره
(711) And when missed prayers are many, specification of each prayer is required. If he intends to facilitate the matter, he should intend the first Zuhr upon him or the last.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This ruling addresses the practical difficulty when a person has missed many prayers of the same type (e.g., many Zuhr prayers). The author states that one must specify which particular prayer is being made up (e.g., the Zuhr of a specific day). However, for ease, one may simply intend 'the first Zuhr' that is due upon him or 'the last Zuhr'. This is sufficient. The Urdu commentary elaborates that if only one prayer is missed, no detailed specification is needed; but if many are missed, specification is necessary. The facilitation of intending first or last is accepted.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yīn): Specification; identifying which particular missed prayer is being performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Intend the exact date of each prayer.
B) Intend the first Zuhr upon him or the last Zuhr.
C) Intend any Zuhr without specification.
D) Intend a different prayer like 'Asr.

Key Takeaway
Multiple missed prayers require specification, but intending the first or last of the type is a valid facilitation.
