The Priority of Tawhid in Da'wa: Mu'adh's Mission to Yemen
Prophetic instruction on prioritising da'wa: first tawhid, then prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of da'wa to non-Muslims and identify the proof from the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
Da'wa must begin with tawhid; then the obligation of prayer is to be announced.

This lesson examines a prophetic instruction that establishes the fundamental order of calling others to Islam. The hadith of Mu'adh (RA) serves as a key evidence (wajh) for prioritising tawhid before detailing religious obligations. It is cited in Hanafi fiqh works to support the obligation of prayer and the methodology of da'wa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is da'wa (calling non-Muslims to Islam). The ruling derived from this hadith is that the caller must start with tawhid (worship of Allah alone) before informing about the obligation of prayer.
The hadith is used as a proof for the wajib nature of this order.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith of Mu'adh narrated by Ibn Abbas (RA), found in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections. It is a hadith ahad (single-narrator) but accepted as evidence.
The text states: 'عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله لما بعث معاذا الى اليمن قال...'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet explicitly instructs: 'Let the first thing you call them to be the worship of Allah' (فليكن اول ما تدعوهم اليه عبادة الله). This command uses the imperative 'فليكن', which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub. Then after they recognize Allah, inform them about the five prayers. The sequential order is clear.
The phrase 'فاذا عرفوا الله فأخبرهم' makes the second step conditional upon the first.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among the four schools regarding the priority of tawhid in da'wa. However, some may differ on whether the order is obligatory (wajib) or merely recommended (sunnah). The Hanafi school leans towards wajib based on the imperative.
The majority of scholars consider it mustahabb to follow this order, but Hanafi usul gives weight to the imperative.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that da'wa must begin with tawhid, then the obligation of prayer. This is supported by the explicit wording of the hadith and is cited in core Hanafi texts like al-Hidayah.
The hadith also establishes the wujub (obligation) of the five daily prayers, as it says 'أن الله فرض عليهم خمس صلوات'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه : عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الله لما بعث معاذا الى اليمن قال انک تقدم علی قوم اهل کتاب فليكن اول ما تدعوهم اليه عبادة الله عز و جل فاذا عرفوا الله فأخبرهم ان الله فرض عليهم خمس صلوات
Evidence: From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah, when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen, said: 'You are going to a people of the Book. Let the first thing you call them to be the worship of Allah Almighty. When they recognize Allah, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them five prayers.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This hadith is cited as a proof (wajh/evidence) for the ruling that da'wa should begin with tawhid, and then the obligation of prayer. It may be used to support the chapter on qaḍā' by establishing the fundamental obligation of prayer. The hadith is from Ibn Abbas, transmitted by Bukhari and others. The text shows that the Prophet prioritized tawhid first, then informed about the obligation of prayers.

Key Terms
وجہ (wajh): Evidence or proof, often a hadith cited as support for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The obligation of the five daily prayers
B) The worship of Allah alone (tawhid)
C) The payment of zakah
D) The observance of fasting

Key Takeaway
The prophetic methodology for da'wa begins with establishing tawhid before introducing the obligations of Islam.

Intending Numerous Missed Prayers: The Hanafi Concession
Ruling on specification of numerous missed prayers with concession for ease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying numerous missed prayers and apply the relaxation of intending the first or last prayer of that type.

Core Idea
When many prayers are missed, intend the first or last of its kind — ease over exact specification.

Making up missed prayers (qada) is a wajib duty. But what if you have missed many Zuhrs from different days? Specifying each exact day could be impossible. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi concession: you may intend the first Zuhr upon your responsibility or the last Zuhr, and the same principle extends to missed fasts. We will also see the rule of thumb: fewer than six missed prayers preserve the obligation of order; six or more lift it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation to specify
The matn states that when missed prayers are numerous, each requires specification (ta'yin). Understand that this is the default rule: the intention must pinpoint a specific fard to be valid.
Without specification, the intention is ambiguous and the prayer may not count.
2
Apply the relaxation for ease
If one desires ease, they may intend the first Zuhr upon their responsibility or the last Zuhr. This covers all missed Zuhrs without needing to remember each day.
This is a rukhsa (concession) to avoid hardship.
3
Link to the principle of order (tartib)
The commentary explains a key rule: as long as fewer than six prayers are missed, one must maintain order (e.g., make up the oldest first). After six missed, order is no longer required, and one may even pray the current time's prayer before completing qada.
The threshold of six is specific to the Hanafi school.
4
Derive the mufta bihi position
The operative fatwa: for less than six missed prayers, specification of exact prayer and order are wajib. For six or more, specification is relaxed (first or last suffices) and order is not required.
This is the position of the later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا كثرت الفوائت يحتاج لتعيين كل صلوة فان اراد تسهيل الامر علیه نوی اول ظهر عليه و آخره (۱۲) وكذا الصوم من رمضانين على احد تصحيحين مختلفين (۷۱۳) ويعذر من اسلم بدار الحرب بجهله الشرائع. اصول : چھ نماز فوت ہونے سے پہلے صاحب ترتیب رہتا ہے، اور مجموعہ چھ نمازیں فوت ہو گئیں تو یہ صاحب ترتیب نہیں رہا اس لئے اسکے لئے وقتیہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ترجمه : (۷۱) اور جب فوت شدہ نمازیں زیادہ ہو جائیں تو ہر ایک نماز کے معین کرنے کی ضرورت ہوگی ۔ اب اگر آسانی چاہے تو ( مثلا ) اول ظہر اپنے ذمہ یا آخر ظہر کی نیت کرے۔ تشریح : مثلا ایک نماز فوت ہوئی ہو تو اتنی نیت کافی ہے کہ فوت شدہ نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں لیکن اگر بہت سارے ظہر فوت ہوئی ہوں تو کس دن کی ظہر ادا کر رہا ہے یہ پتہ نہیں ہے اس لئے دن کے تعین کی ضرورت پڑے گی ۔ البتہ آسانی کے لئے یہ نیت کرلے پہلی ظہر ادا کر رہا ہوں یا آخری ظہر ادا کر رہا ہوں ، ایسی نیت بھی کافی ہے۔
And when missed prayers become numerous, each prayer needs to be specified. If he wants to ease the matter, he may intend the first Zuhr upon him or the last. And likewise the fast of two Ramadans according to one of two different corrections. And one who accepts Islam in the Abode of War is excused due to ignorance of the laws. Principle: Before six prayers are missed, one remains the master of order; if six prayers are missed, he is no longer master of order, so it is permissible for him to pray the current time's prayer. Translation: (71) And when missed prayers become many, each prayer needs to be specified. Now if he wants ease, he may intend the first Zuhr upon his responsibility or the last Zuhr. Clarification: For example, if one prayer was missed, the intention that he is praying the missed prayer is sufficient. But if many Zuhr prayers are missed, he does not know which day's Zuhr he is performing, so he needs to specify the day. However, for ease, he may intend 'I am performing the first Zuhr' or 'I am performing the last Zuhr' – such an intention is also sufficient.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the chapter on making up missed prayers. The matn states that when a large number of prayers are missed, one must specify which prayer is being performed. However, to facilitate, one may intend the first or last of the type of prayer (e.g., first Zuhr or last Zuhr). The same principle applies to missed fasts of two Ramadans, with a difference of opinion. A person who accepts Islam in a non-Muslim land is excused for ignorance of the laws. The explanation clarifies that as long as fewer than six prayers are missed, one must maintain order; but if six or more are missed, order is no longer required, and one may pray the current time's prayer instead of making up missed ones first.

Key Terms
فوائت (fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that are to be made up (qada).
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the exact prayer (e.g., which day's Zuhr) in one's intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has missed many Zuhr prayers from different days, which intention is sufficient according to the ease provided?
A) Intending the exact date and day of the missed prayer
B) Intending the first Zuhr or the last Zuhr
C) Intending any missed prayer without specification
D) Intending the current time's prayer

Key Takeaway
When missed prayers are numerous (six or more), one may intend the first or last of that type of prayer for ease, and order is no longer required.

Excuse for New Muslim in Dar al-Harb
Ruling with proof from Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused for ignorance of Sharia, identify the dalil (hadith of Mu'adh), and explain its wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
A new Muslim in enemy territory is excused for missing details; the hadith of Mu'adh proves gradual teaching excuses prior ignorance.

This passage addresses a crucial distinction: not all Muslims face the same level of accountability. A person who accepts Islam in dār al-ḥarb (land of war) is excused for ignorance of detailed Sharia rulings because they lack access to scholars and teaching. The proof is the famous hadith where the Prophet sent Mu‘ādh to Yemen, showing that obligations are taught step by step, and until a person is taught, their ignorance is excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a new Muslim living in dār al-ḥarb. The ruling is that they are excused (rukhṣah) from liability for failing to perform secondary obligations due to ignorance.
Primary obligations like tawhid are not excused – only subsidiary (furū‘) rulings.
2
Locate the dalīl
The text cites the hadith of Mu‘ādh ibn Jabal (ra) when the Prophet sent him to Yemen. This hadith is found in Ṣaḥīḥ Muslim.
The hadith is aḥad (single-chain) but accepted as proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The Prophet instructed Mu‘ādh to first call people to tawḥīd, then to prayer, then to zakāt. This step-by-step teaching implies that those who have not yet been taught are not held accountable for the obligations they do not know.
The logical inference is that ignorance before teaching is an excuse.
4
Note the scope of the excuse
The excuse applies only to subsidiary rulings (fatāwā) – not to the fundamentals of Islam which every convert must know. Also, the excuse is tied to lack of access to knowledge.
If the Muslim later gains access to knowledge and remains ignorant, the excuse may lapse.
5
Evaluate the authority weight
This ruling is from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (core Hanafi texts) and is considered muftā bihi. The cross-madhhab status is muttafaq ‘alayh – all schools accept the general principle.
The dalīl is zannī al-thubūt but qaṭ‘ī al-dalālah in its implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعذر من اسلم بدار الحرب بجهله الشرائع. وجه : عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الله لما بعث معاذا الى اليمن قال انک تقدم علی قوم اهل کتاب فليكن اول ما تدعوهم اليه عبادة الله عز و جل فاذا عرفوا الله فأخبرهم ان الله فرض عليهم خمس صلوات في يومهم وليلتهم فاذا فعلوا فأخبرهم ان الله قد فرض عليهم زكاة تؤخذ من اموالهم فترد على فقرائهم فاذا اطاعوا بها فخذ منهم و توق كرائم اموالهم - (مسلم شریف ، باب الدعا الی الشھادتین ،ص۳۲، نمبر ۱۲۳/۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے کلمہ سکھلاؤ پھر نماز کا حکم دو، اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب میں جزوی مسئلے کی جہالت قابل قبول ہے۔
And one who accepts Islam in the Abode of War is excused due to ignorance of the laws. Proof: From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah, when he sent Mu'adh to Yemen, said: 'You are going to a people of the Book. So let the first thing you call them to be the worship of Allah Almighty. When they know Allah, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them five prayers in their day and night. When they do that, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them zakat to be taken from their wealth and given to their poor. If they obey you in that, take from them and avoid their valuable wealth.' (Muslim, Chapter on Invitation to the Two Shahadahs, p. 32, no. 123/19). In this hadith, it says: first teach the kalimah, then command prayer. From this it is known that in dar al-harb, ignorance of subsidiary issues is acceptable.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that a person who accepts Islam in dar al-harb (land of war) is excused for ignorance of Sharia rulings. The proof is the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when he was sent to Yemen. The hadith shows the gradual teaching of Islam: first tawhid, then prayer, then zakat. This implies that until a person has access to teaching, he is not held accountable for subsidiary rulings. The commentary concludes that in dar al-harb, ignorance of specific issues is excusable due to lack of educational facilities.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Land under non-Muslim rule, where Muslims may be unable to learn all Sharia rulings.
معذور (ma'dhur): Excused from liability due to valid reason (ignorance).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Rational reasoning that ignorance is always an excuse
D) The Quranic verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity'

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Mu'adh establishes that in dar al-harb, ignorance of subsidiary rulings is excused due to lack of teaching.

The Duty to Join the Congregation: Leaving Individual Prayer for Jama'ah
Introduction to the chapter on joining congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving a sunnah or fard prayer to join the jama'ah and cite the two hadith proofs that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
The congregation takes precedence over individual prayer – leave any prayer to join jama'ah.

This lesson introduces a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh: the obligation to prioritize congregational prayer over any individual prayer. The source text derives this from the severe warning about missing jama'ah and the explicit prohibition of praying any nafl after the iqamah. We will examine the two key hadith and their implications for a person who has already begun a prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling Scenario
The text presents three situations: (1) if the fard is being prayed in jama'ah, join them and leave your own prayer; (2) if you have already prayed your fard alone, join the jama'ah again – that prayer becomes nafl and your original fard remains; (3) if you are praying a sunnah, leave it and join the jama'ah.
The key is that jama'ah overrides any current individual prayer.
2
Examine the First Hadith: Warning against Missing Jama'ah
Read the hadith of Abu Huraira where the Prophet (ﷺ) considered burning houses of those who miss jama'ah. This indicates the severe importance and near-obligation of attending jama'ah.
Though the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), its meaning is clear and supported by other evidence.
3
Examine the Second Hadith: Prohibition of Nafl after Iqamah
The hadith 'When the iqamah is said, there is no prayer except the obligatory one' directly prohibits any non-obligatory prayer once iqamah has started. This includes continuing a sunnah you have already begun.
The phrasing 'لا صلوة' is general and includes all nafl prayers.
4
Derive the Ruling from the Proofs
Combine the two proofs: the first establishes the importance of jama'ah, the second explicitly prohibits other prayers during iqamah. Therefore, one must break any current prayer (sunnah or even a fard started alone) to join the jama'ah.
If one breaks a fard prayer, that fard is not invalidated; instead, the intention is changed to nafl, and the original fard remains valid after repeating with jama'ah.
5
Apply the Ruling in Practice
For a muqtadi: if you enter the masjid and find the imam praying, join immediately. If you have started a sunnah, break it with the intention to join. If you have prayed your fard alone, join again and count it as nafl.
The mufta bihi position is to always join jama'ah, even if it means breaking a current prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة ضروری نوٹ : اس باب کے مسائل اس قاعدہ سے مستنبط ہے کہ اگر فرض نماز جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی جارہی ہو تو اس میں شریک ہونا چاہئے اور اپنی نماز چھوڑ دینی چاہئے ، اور اگر فرض پڑھ چکا ہوتو دوبارہ جماعت کے ساتھ شامل ہو جانا چاہئے ، یہ نماز نفل ہوگی اور پہلے پڑھی ہوئی نماز فرض برقرار رہے گی ۔ اور اگر سنت پڑھ رہا ہوتو اسکو چھوڑ کر جماعت میں شریک ہو جانا چاہئے ۔ وجه : اسکی وجہ یہ ہے جماعت کی ایک اہمیت ہے اسکے لئے یہ حدیث ہے (۱) ۔ عن ابي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال (( و الذي نفسي بيده لقد هممت ان آمر بحطب ليحطب ثم آمر بالصلوة فيؤذن لهاثم آمر رجلا فيؤم الناس ، ثم أخالف الى رجال فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم ، و الذي نفسي بيده ! لو يعلم أحدهم أنه يجد عرقا سمينا ، أو مــرمـاتين حسنتين لشهد العشاء ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب وجوب صلوة الجماعة، ص ۸۹ نمبر ۶۴۴ مسلم شریف ، باب فضا فضل صلوة الجماعة و بيان التشديد فى التخلف عنها وأنها فرض كفایة ، ص ۲۶۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۱/۶۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت کے ساتھ شریک ہونا چاہئے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : (( اذا أقيمت الصلوة فلا صلوة الا المكتوبة)) مسلم شریف، باب كراهية الشروع في نافلة بعد شروع المؤذن في اقامة الصلوة ، الخ، ص ۲۸۸، نمبر ۱۶۴۴/۷۱۰ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء اذا اقیمت الصلوۃ فلا صلوۃ الا المكتوبة ، ص ۱۱۳ نمبر (۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض نماز کی اقامت کہی جارہی ہو تو کوئی نماز نہ پڑھے، بلکہ فرض ہی پڑھے۔
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Necessary Note: The issues of this chapter are derived from the principle that if the obligatory prayer is being performed in congregation, one should join it and leave his own prayer. And if he has already prayed the obligatory, he should join the congregation again; this prayer will be supererogatory and his previous obligatory prayer remains valid. And if he is praying a sunnah prayer, he should leave it and join the congregation. Proof: The reason is that congregation has great importance, and for this there is this hadith: (1) From Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: 'By the One in Whose hand is my soul, I almost resolved to order firewood to be gathered, then order the prayer and the iqamah be said, then order a man to lead the people, then go to some men and burn their houses down. By the One in Whose hand is my soul! If any of them knew that he would find a fat bone or two good pieces of meat, he would attend the Isha prayer.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Obligation of Congregational Prayer, p. 89, no. 644; Muslim, Chapter on Virtue of Congregational Prayer and Severity for Missing It, p. 262, no. 1381/65). From this hadith it is known that one should join the congregation. (2) From Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: 'When the iqamah is said, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' (Muslim, Chapter on Dislike of Beginning a Nafl after the Mu'adhin Begins Iqamah, p. 288, no. 1644/710; Tirmidhi, Chapter on When Iqamah is Said There is No Prayer Except the Obligatory, p. 113, no. 42). This hadith states that when iqamah for the obligatory prayer is being said, one should not pray any other prayer but the obligatory.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This is the introduction to the chapter on catching the fard prayer. It states a fundamental qa'idah: the established congregational prayer takes precedence over any individual prayer. The text then provides the proofs: (1) the severe warning about missing jama'ah from the hadith of Abu Huraira, and (2) the explicit command that after iqamah, only the fard prayer should be performed. This establishes the supremacy of jama'ah and the obligation to join it.

Key Terms
ادراك الفريضة (idrak al-faridah): Catching the obligatory prayer; joining the congregation for the fard prayer.
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam, considered highly recommended (wajib in the view of some Hanafis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The iqamah does not affect the validity of ongoing prayers.

Key Takeaway
Joining the congregation takes precedence over any individual prayer; break your current prayer to join jama'ah.

When to Break an Individual Fard to Join Congregation
Ruling on breaking an individual fard to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a Hanafi must break an individual fard prayer to join the congregation and apply it to different prayer lengths.

Core Idea
If you haven't completed one rak'ah, break; else, rules differ by prayer type.

The Hanafi school permits breaking an obligatory prayer for a weightier reason: joining the congregation. However, this permission is not unconditional. This lesson examines the precise scenario when breaking is required and how the ruling changes based on how much of the prayer has been completed and the type of prayer being offered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger event
Determine the moment when the congregation for the same fard prayer is established (iqamah) while you are already praying that fard alone.
This triggers the evaluation of whether to break.
2
Check rak'ah completion
Ask: Have you performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah? If not, you have not completed one full rak'ah.
Completing sajdah of the first rak'ah marks the completion of one rak'ah.
3
Apply the general rule
If you have not completed one rak'ah, break your prayer and join the congregation regardless of whether it is a 2, 3, or 4 rak'ah prayer.
4
Differentiate by prayer length if rak'ah completed
If you have completed one rak'ah (i.e., performed sajdah) and the prayer is not a 4-rak'ah fard (i.e., it is 2 or 3 rak'ah), you must still break and join. If it is a 4-rak'ah prayer, do not break; continue as nafl or complete as normal? The text implies you should not break.
The source text explicitly states: 'if in a prayer other than four-rak'ah he has also performed sajdah, he should still break it.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Since he has not completed one rak'ah, and the prayer is based on rak'ahs, whether he is praying a four-rak'ah prayer or a two-rak'ah one, in every case he should break the prayer and join the congregation. Commentary
This is the detailed ruling on breaking an individual fard prayer to join the congregation. The matn (numbered 714) is given in Urdu translation. The ruling states that if one starts a fard prayer alone and the congregation for the same fard starts, he must break his prayer if he has not yet performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah (i.e., has not completed one full rak'ah). If he has performed sajdah in the first rak'ah, the ruling depends on the type of prayer. The commentary then breaks down four scenarios. The first scenario is as mentioned: if he has not completed one rak'ah, he breaks regardless of whether the prayer is 2 or 4 rak'ahs. The second scenario (cut off in OCR) likely deals with when he has completed one or more rak'ahs.

سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration; in this context, completing sajdah of the first rak'ah marks the completion of one rak'ah.
قطع (qat'): Breaking the prayer before completion.

General Ruling on Joining the Congregation While Alone in Fard
Introduction and first scenario of catching the fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a fard prayer to join the congregation and apply the distinction between four-rak'ah and non-four-rak'ah prayers.

Core Idea
Congregation takes precedence: break your individual fard to join, unless it's a four-rak'ah prayer after sajdah.

This passage from the classical Hanafi matn addresses a common scenario: you have started your obligatory prayer alone, and then the congregation for the same prayer begins. What should you do? The Hanafi school, prioritizing the communal obligation, provides a clear ruling based on the strength of the hadith evidence. In this lesson, you will work through the two key scenarios and understand the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is starting a fard prayer alone when the congregation for the same fard is established. The ruling is that one must break his individual prayer and follow the imam, with a condition regarding the prostration.
The matn says 'قطع واقتدى' (cut off and follow).
2
Locate the supporting dalil
Two hadith are cited: the 'burning houses' hadith emphasizing the importance of congregation, and the hadith 'When the iqamah is given, no prayer except the obligatory.' Both prove the emphasis on congregation over individual prayer.
The dalil is ahad but zanni al-thubut, yet sufficient for wajib.
3
Understand the condition regarding sajdah
The ruling distinguishes between having performed the sajdah of the current rak'ah or not, and whether the prayer is four-rak'ah (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) or not (Fajr, Maghrib). For non-four-rak'ah, even after sajdah one breaks; for four-rak'ah, one breaks only if sajdah has not been performed.
If sajdah is done, the rak'ah is complete; for a four-rak'ah prayer, breaking would forfeit a complete unit.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: after sajdah in a four-rak'ah prayer, one does NOT break, but for Fajr/Maghrib one still breaks. This is unique to Hanafis; Shafi'is generally prohibit breaking any fard once started.
Cross-madhhab awareness is important for muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة (۷۱۴) اذا شرع في فرض منفردا فاقيمت الجماعة قطع واقتدى ان لم يسجد لما شرع فيه او في غير رباعية

ضروری نوٹ : اس باب کے مسائل اس قاعدہ سے مستنبط ہے کہ اگر فرض نماز جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھی جارہی ہو تو اس میں شریک ہونا چاہئے اور اپنی نماز چھوڑ دینی چاہئے ، اور اگر فرض پڑھ چکا ہوتو دوبارہ جماعت کے ساتھ شامل ہو جانا چاہئے ، یہ نماز نفل ہوگی اور پہلے پڑھی ہوئی نماز فرض برقرار رہے گی ۔ اور اگر سنت پڑھ رہا ہوتو اسکو چھوڑ کر جماعت میں شریک ہو جانا چاہئے ۔ وجه : اسکی وجہ یہ ہے جماعت کی ایک اہمیت ہے اسکے لئے یہ حدیث ہے (۱) ۔ عن ابي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال (( و الذي نفسي بيده لقد هممت ان آمر بحطب ليحطب ثم آمر بالصلوة فيؤذن لهاثم آمر رجلا فيؤم الناس ، ثم أخالف الى رجال فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم ، و الذي نفسي بيده ! لو يعلم أحدهم أنه يجد عرقا سمينا ، أو مــرمـاتين حسنتين لشهد العشاء ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب وجوب صلوة الجماعة، ص ۸۹ نمبر ۶۴۴ مسلم شریف ، باب فضا فضل صلوة الجماعة و بيان التشديد فى التخلف عنها وأنها فرض كفایة ، ص ۲۶۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۱/۶۵ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جماعت کے ساتھ شریک ہونا چاہئے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : (( اذا أقيمت الصلوة فلا صلوة الا المكتوبة)) مسلم شریف، باب كراهية الشروع في نافلة بعد شروع المؤذن في اقامة الصلوة ، الخ، ص ۲۸۸، نمبر ۱۶۴۴/۷۱۰ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء اذا اقیمت الصلوۃ فلا صلوۃ الا المكتوبة ، ص ۱۱۳ نمبر (۴۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض نماز کی اقامت کہی جارہی ہو تو کوئی نماز نہ پڑھے، بلکہ فرض ہی پڑھے۔

ترجمه : ( ۱۴ ) اگر فرض نماز کیلے شروع کرتے ہوئے جماعت کھڑی ہو جائے تو اگر اپنی شروع کی ہوئی نماز کا سجدہ نہ کرلیا ہو، یا اگر چار رکعت والی نماز کے سوا دوسری نماز میں سجدہ بھی کر لیا ہوتب بھی اس کو تو ڑ کر امام کے ساتھ اقتدا کرے۔

تشریح : یہاں چار صورتیں ہیں [1] پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ وہی فرض پڑھ رہا تھا جسکی جماعت کھڑی ہوئی اور ابھی پہلی رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے کہ جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو چونکہ ابھی ایک رکعت پوری نہیں ہے، اور نماز بتیر انہیں بنی ہے اس لئے چاہے چار رکعت والی نماز پڑھ رہا ہو چاہے دو رکعت والی ہر حال میں نماز توڑ دے اور جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دو رکعت والا فرض پڑھ رہا تھا اور سجدہ کر لیا تو اس کو توڑ کر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے، کیونکہ دوسری رکعت ملائے گا تو فرض پورا ہو جائے گا ، اور جماعت رہ جائے گی ۔
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. (714) If one begins a fard prayer alone and then the congregation is established, he cuts off and follows (the imam) if he has not prostrated for what he began, or in a non-four-rak'ah (prayer).

Important Note: The issues of this chapter are derived from this rule: if the fard prayer is being performed with congregation, one should join it and leave his own prayer; and if he has already prayed the fard, he should join the congregation again, and that prayer will be nafl and the first prayer remains as fard. And if he was praying sunnah, he should leave it and join the congregation. Reason: The importance of congregation is indicated by this hadith...

Translation: (714) If one starts a fard prayer and the congregation stands up, then if he has not performed the prostration of his started prayer, or if in other than a four-rak'ah prayer even if he has performed prostration, he should break it and follow the imam.

Explanation: There are four scenarios: [1] The first scenario is that he was praying the same fard for which the congregation is established and he has not yet performed the prostration of the first rak'ah; since one rak'ah is not complete, and the prayer is based on units, whether it is a four-rak'ah or two-rak'ah prayer, in all cases he breaks the prayer and joins the congregation. [2] The second scenario is that he was praying a two-rak'ah fard and he performed the prostration; then he should break it and join the congregation, because he will add a second rak'ah and complete the fard, but the congregation will be lost.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the situation where a person begins an obligatory prayer alone and then the congregational prayer for the same fard is established. The author presents the ruling in Arabic (matn) and then provides an Urdu commentary. The key principle is that the congregation takes precedence over individual prayer. The ruling distinguishes between two cases: (1) if the person has not yet performed the prostration of the current rak'ah, he should break his prayer immediately and join the congregation, regardless of whether it is a 2- or 4-rak'ah prayer; (2) if it is a non-4-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Fajr or Maghrib) and he has already performed the prostration, he should still break his prayer and join. The hadith cited emphasize the obligation of attending congregation and that once the iqamah is given, no other prayer should be offered except the obligatory one.

Key Terms
ادراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Catching the obligatory prayer in congregation by joining the imam, even if one has started it alone.
غير رباعية (ghayr rubā'iyyah): A prayer that is not four rak'ahs, i.e., two-rak'ah (Fajr) or three-rak'ah (Maghrib) prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a person is praying the Maghrib prayer (3 rak'ahs) alone and has performed the sajdah of the second rak'ah, and the congregation for Maghrib begins, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Break his prayer and join the congregation.
B) Complete his prayer alone without joining.
C) Add a third rak'ah and then join the congregation.
D) Ignore the congregation and continue.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires breaking a non-4-rak'ah fard prayer at any point to join the congregation, but for 4-rak'ah prayers, breaking is only required before the first sajdah of the current rak'ah.

Four-Rak'ah Prayer with One Sajdah: Make Two Rak'ahs Nafl Then Join
Specific ruling for a four-rak'ah prayer when sajdah was performed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a four-rak'ah fard prayer when sajdah has been performed and explain the procedure to convert the performed rak'ahs into nafl and join the congregation.

Core Idea
Complete two rak'ahs with salām as nafl, then join the congregation – preserve your prayer and the reward of jamā'ah.

Sometimes you begin a four-rak'ah fard prayer alone, perform the sajdah of the first rak'ah, and then the congregation for the same prayer commences. What should you do? Simply breaking the prayer invalidates it (since one rak'ah is complete), but continuing alone means missing the congregation. Hanafi fiqh provides a precise solution: add a second rak'ah to make a two-rak'ah nafl, complete it with tasleem, and then join the imam for the fard. This ruling balances both benefits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a person has started a four-rak'ah fard prayer (Zuhr, 'Asr, or 'Ishā') alone and has performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah (i.e., completed one full rak'ah).
The prayer cannot be nullified arbitrarily because one rak'ah with sajdah is a valid unit.
2
Determine the required action
He must add one more rak'ah (making a total of two rak'ahs), recite tashahhud, and say salām. This transforms the two rak'ahs into a nafl prayer.
The intention of the original fard prayer is abandoned; the two rak'ahs become supererogatory.
3
Understand the consequence
After completing the two rak'ahs as nafl, he should renew the intention for the fard prayer and join the congregation in whatever posture the imam is in.
He does not need to repeat the rak'ah he already performed; the fard prayer will be prayed anew with the imam.
4
Recognize the rationale
The ruling is based on the strong recommendation of congregation (wujūb al-jamā'ah) and the principle that a prayer once started cannot be invalidated without proper conclusion.
The proof is the general command to join the congregation and the hadith prohibiting supererogatory prayers after iqāmah, but here the performed rak'ah is converted into nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۱۵) وان سجد في رباعية ضمّ ركعة ثانية وسلّم لتصير الركعتان له نافلة ثم ركعت والی

ترجمه : (۷۱۵) اور چار رکعت والی نماز میں اگر سجدہ کر لیا ہو تو ایک دوسری رکعت ملا کر سلام پھیر لے ، تا کہ یہ دواس کے لئے نفل ہو جائے، پھر فرض کی نیت سے امام کے ساتھ اقتدا کر لے۔

تشریح : ی اوپر کی تیسری صورت ہے۔ مثلاظہر، یا عر، یا عشاء کی چار رکعت والی نماز تھی اور پہلی رکعت پر سجدہ کر لیا تو دوسری رکعت ملالے اور سلام پھیر دے، تا کہ یہ دورکعت نفل ہو جائے اور فرض کی نیت سے امام کے ساتھ شامل ہو جائے۔

وجه : تاکہ نفل بھی ہو جائے اور جماعت میں بھی شرکت ہو جائے۔
(715) And if he prostrated in a four-rak'ah prayer, he should add a second rak'ah and say salām, so that the two rak'ahs become nafl for him, then he should join (the imam).

Translation: (715) And if in a four-rak'ah prayer he has performed prostration, he should add a second rak'ah and say salām, so that these two become nafl for him, then he should follow the imam with the intention of fard.

Explanation: This is the third scenario above. For example, if it was a four-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr, 'Asr, or 'Ishā', and he performed prostration on the first rak'ah, then he should add a second rak'ah and say salām, so that these two rak'ahs become nafl and he joins the imam with the intention of fard.

Reason: So that he attains both the nafl and the congregation.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a specific ruling for a person who has started a four-rak'ah fard prayer alone and has performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah. Since he has completed one full rak'ah (by sajdah), the prayer cannot be broken arbitrarily. Instead, he should add one more rak'ah to make two rak'ahs, complete them with tasleem, and then join the congregation for the fard prayer. The two rak'ahs count as nafl. This preserves his performed rak'ahs as a non-obligatory prayer while allowing him to join the congregation.

Key Terms
رباعية (rubā'iyyah): A four-rak'ah prayer, specifically the fard prayers of Zuhr, 'Asr, and 'Ishā'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts Zuhr prayer alone, performs sajdah in the first rak'ah, and then the congregation for Zuhr begins, what should he do?
A) Break the prayer immediately and join the congregation.
B) Complete two rak'ahs with salām and then join the congregation with the intention of fard.
C) Complete all four rak'ahs and then join the congregation as nafl.
D) Continue his prayer alone and ignore the congregation.

Key Takeaway
When sajdah is performed in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, it is wajib to complete two rak'ahs as nafl and then join the congregation.

Completing Three Rak'ahs: Finish Fard Then Join as Nafl
Ruling for when one has completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard alone and then a congregation begins, and identify the exception for 'Asr and Fajr.

Core Idea
Complete your fard first, then join the congregation as nafl — but not after 'Asr or Fajr.

A common scenario: you are partway through a four-rak'ah fard prayer alone, and then a congregation starts. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on how many rak'ahs you have completed. This lesson addresses the situation where you have already performed three rak'ahs. You must finish your fard, then you may join the congregation as a nafl prayer — except when the prayer is 'Asr or Fajr, because nafl at those times is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person has completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Ishā') alone. The congregation for the same prayer begins.
The ruling only applies when three rak'ahs have been completed; different rulings apply for one or two rak'ahs.
2
Determine the primary ruling
The person must complete the fourth rak'ah to finish the fard. Then he should join the congregation with the intention of nafl.
The fard is prioritized; joining as nafl is recommended but not obligatory.
3
Apply the exception for 'Asr and Fajr
If the prayer is 'Asr, the person should complete the fard but NOT join as nafl because nafl after 'Asr is makruh tahrimi. The same applies for Fajr: after completing the two-rak'ah fard, do not join.
This exception is derived from the prohibition of nafl during these times.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith of Jabir ibn Yazid al-Aswad: the Prophet said that if one has already prayed in his place and then finds the imam, he should pray with him and it will be nafl. This is the basis for joining as nafl after completing the fard.
The hadith is ahad but accepted; the Hanafi school uses it for this ruling.

Source Text

(۷۱۶) وان صلى ثلاثا اتمها ثم اقتدى بنية النفل في غير العصر

ترجمه : (۷۱۶) اور اگر تین رکعت پڑھ لی ہو تو اس کو پورا کر کے پھر عصر کے سوا دوسری نمازوں میں نفل کی نیت سے امام کے ساتھ اقتدا کرلے۔

تشریح : اوپر کی چوتھی صورت ہے۔ اگر چار رکعت والی نماز تھی اور تین رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو چوتھی رکعت ملا کر فرض پوری کرلے، اور بعد میں نفل کے طور پر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ یا دورکعت والا فرض ہو اور دوسری رکعت کا سجدہ کر چکا ہو تو اب اس کو پورا کر لے ، اور چونکہ یہ فجر کی نماز ہے اور فجر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے، اس لئے فرض کرنے کے بعد اب جماعت میں شریک نہ ہو۔

وجه : (1) جماعت کی اہمیت کی حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ (۲) اگر ایک رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو اس کو بچانے کے لئے دوسری رکعت ملائے تا کہ وہ بچ جائے ، اور تین رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو اب قریب قریب فرض پڑھ چکا ہے اس لئے چوتھی رکعت ملا کر فرض پوری کر لے، اور نفل کے طور پر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ (۳) فرض پڑھ چکا ہو اب نفل کے طور پر شریک ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن يزيد الاسود عن ابيه أنه صلى مع رسول الله له و هو غلام شاب .... فقال ما منع كما أن تصليا معنا ؟ قالا : قد صلينا في رحالنا ، فقال لا تفعلوا اذا صلى أحدكم في رحله ثم أدرك الامام ولم يصل فليصل معه فانها له نافلة - ابوداود شریف ، باب فیمن صلی فی منزلہ ثم ادرک الجماعة یصلی متخصم ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۵۷۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر فرض ایک مرتبہ پڑھ چکا ہو دوبارہ جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو اسکے ساتھ دوبارہ نماز پڑھ لے اور یہ نماز نفل ہوگی۔
(716) And if he prayed three rak'ahs, he should complete it (the fourth) and then follow (the imam) with the intention of nafl in other than 'Asr.

Translation: (716) And if he has prayed three rak'ahs, then he should complete it, and then join the congregation with the intention of nafl in prayers other than 'Asr.

Explanation: This is the fourth scenario above. If it was a four-rak'ah prayer and he has prayed three rak'ahs, he should add the fourth rak'ah to complete the fard, and then join the congregation as nafl. Or if it is a two-rak'ah fard (Fajr) and he has performed the prostration of the second rak'ah, then he should complete it (i.e., finish the fard), and because it is Fajr and there is no nafl after Fajr, he should not join the congregation after completing the fard.

Reason: (1) The hadith about the importance of congregation has passed. (2) If he has prayed one rak'ah, he should add another to save it; and if he has prayed three rak'ahs, he is close to completing the fard, so he should add the fourth and complete the fard, then join as nafl. (3) The proof for joining as nafl after completing the fard is the hadith of Jabir ... that if one has prayed in his place and then finds the imam, he should pray with him and it will be nafl for him.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage covers the fourth scenario: a person who has already completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard (like Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Ishā') alone. Since he is near completion, he should add the fourth rak'ah, finish the fard, and then join the congregation as a nafl prayer. However, an exception is made for 'Asr (and by implication Fajr): after 'Asr, no nafl is permitted according to the Hanafi school (except the sunnah before, but after fard, nafl is makruh). Similarly for Fajr, as explained earlier, if he has completed the two rak'ahs (the fard), he should not join because there is no nafl after Fajr. The hadith of Jabir supports the principle that if one has already performed the fard, he can pray again with the imam as nafl.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A voluntary prayer, not obligatory. In this context, it is the prayer performed again with the congregation after already having performed the fard.
عصر ('Asr): The afternoon prayer. Here it is specified that one should not join as nafl after completing the 'Asr fard because nafl after 'Asr is makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has completed three rak'ahs of 'Ishā' prayer alone and then the congregation for 'Ishā' begins, what should he do?
A) Break his prayer and join the congregation immediately.
B) Complete the fourth rak'ah, finish the fard, and then join the congregation as nafl.
C) Complete the fourth rak'ah and then not join the congregation because nafl is not allowed after 'Ishā'.
D) Add two more rak'ahs to make it a nafl prayer and then join the congregation.

Key Takeaway
If you have completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard, complete the fourth, then join as nafl except after 'Asr and Fajr.

Joining the Congregation After Starting Salah Alone: Four Scenarios
Rulings with proof for joining congregation after individual prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scenarios for joining the congregation after starting salah alone and apply the correct ruling for each based on the number of rak'ahs and the prayer type.

Core Idea
If you start salah alone and find the congregation, convert incomplete rak'ahs to nafl and join, except when nafl is prohibited.

This lesson clarifies a common situation: you begin praying individually, then realize the congregation is starting. Instead of missing the congregational reward, the Hanafi school provides a structured way to participate. We will study four scenarios from Thamaratun Najah, each with a distinct ruling, supported by a hadith from Abu Dawud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type and stage
Determine if the prayer is ruba'iyyah (4 rak'ahs) or not (e.g., Fajr), how many rak'ahs you have completed, and whether you have made sajdah in the current rak'ah.
A rak'ah is complete only after sajdah.
2
Apply the rule for non-ruba'iyyah prayers
If the prayer is not four rak'ahs (e.g., Fajr) and you have made sajdah in the current rak'ah, you should break your prayer and join the congregation. If you have completed the fard and it is Fajr, do not join because there is no nafl after Fajr.
Breaking here means ending your prayer intentionally.
3
Apply the rule for ruba'iyyah prayers with one rak'ah completed
If you have prayed one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah fard and have made sajdah, add a second rak'ah, say salam, and make those two rak'ahs nafl. Then join the imam for the fard.
This converts the incomplete prayer into a nafl pair (shaf').
4
Apply the rule for ruba'iyyah prayers with three rak'ahs completed
If you have prayed three rak'ahs, add the fourth rak'ah to complete your fard. Then join the congregation as nafl, except for 'Asr where no nafl is allowed after 'Asr.
The fourth is added to complete the fard; then you join as nafl.
5
Understand the hadith evidence
The proof for joining as nafl after completing fard is the hadith: the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'When any of you prays at home then finds the imam, let him pray with him; it will be nafl for him.' (Abu Dawud).
This hadith is the basis for the concession.

باب ادراك الفريضة سجد في غير رباعيّة (۷۱۵) وان سجد في رباعية ضمّ ركعة ثانية وسلّم لتصير الركعتان له نافلة ثم رکعت والی مثلا فجر کی نماز پڑھ رہا تھا تو سجدہ بھی کر لیا تو اس کو تو ڑ کر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے، کیونکہ دوسری رکعت ملائے گا تو فرض پورا ہو جائے گا ، اور جماعت رہ جائے گی ۔ (۳) تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ چار رکعت والی نماز ہے اور سجدہ کر چکا ہے تو دوسری رکعت ملا لے، یہ دورکعت نفل بن جائے گی ، پھر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ [۴] چار رکعت والی نماز تھی اور تین رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو چوتھی رکعت ملا کر فرض پوری کرلے، اور بعد میں نفل کے طور پر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ یا دورکعت والا فرض ہو اور دوسری رکعت کا سجدہ کر چکا ہو تو اب اس کو پورا کر لے ، اور چونکہ یہ فجر کی نماز ہے اور فجر کے بعد نفل نہیں ہے، اس لئے فرض کرنے کے بعد اب جماعت میں شریک نہ ہو۔ وجه : (1) جماعت کی اہمیت کی حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ (۲) اگر ایک رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو اس کو بچانے کے لئے دوسری رکعت ملائے تا کہ وہ بچ جائے ، اور تین رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے تو اب قریب قریب فرض پڑھ چکا ہے اس لئے چوتھی رکعت ملا کر فرض پوری کر لے، اور نفل کے طور پر جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ (۳) فرض پڑھ چکا ہو اب نفل کے طور پر شریک ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔عن جابر بن يزيد الاسود عن ابيه أنه صلى مع رسول الله له و هو غلام شاب .... فقال ما منع كما أن تصليا معنا ؟ قالا : قد صلينا في رحالنا ، فقال لا تفعلوا اذا صلى أحدكم في رحله ثم أدرك الامام ولم يصل فليصل معه فانها له نافلة - Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. He made sajdah in a non-four-rak'ah prayer (715). And if he made sajdah in a four-rak'ah prayer, he should add a second rak'ah and say salam so that the two rak'ahs become nafl for him. Then he should do ruku'... For example, he was praying Fajr prayer and also made sajdah, then he should break it and join the congregation, because he will join a second rak'ah so the fard will be completed, and the congregation will be missed. (3) The third case is that it is a four-rak'ah prayer and he has made sajdah, so he should add a second rak'ah, these two rak'ahs will become nafl, then he should join the congregation. [4] It was a four-rak'ah prayer and he has prayed three rak'ahs, so he should add the fourth rak'ah and complete the fard, and then after that join the congregation as nafl. Or if it is a two-rak'ah fard and he has made the sajdah of the second rak'ah, then he should complete it, and because this is the Fajr prayer and there is no nafl after Fajr, so after performing the fard he should not join the congregation. Justification: (1) The hadith on the importance of congregation has passed earlier. (2) If he has prayed one rak'ah, he should add a second to preserve it, and if he has prayed three rak'ah, then he has almost completed the fard, so he should add the fourth and complete the fard, then join the congregation as nafl. (3) If he has completed the fard, then joining as nafl: its proof is this hadith: From Jabir ibn Yazid al-Aswad from his father that he prayed with the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) while he was a young boy... then he said: 'What prevented you two from praying with us?' They said: 'We have prayed in our dwellings.' He said: 'Do not do that. When any of you prays in his dwelling then finds the imam and has not prayed, let him pray with him, for it will be nafl for him.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who prays at home then catches the congregation, ... p.195 no.575). In this hadith, if one has prayed the fard once and the congregation is established again, he should pray again with them, and this prayer will be nafl. Lexicon: If sajdah is done, one rak'ah is completed. And before sajdah, the rak'ah is not complete, so as if no particular deficiency occurred. But if sajdah is done, one rak'ah is complete, so he should add a second rak'ah to make a pair, and complete one prayer. Ruba'iyyah: four-rak'ah prayer. Translation: (715) And in a four-rak'ah prayer, if he has made sajdah, he should add a second rak'ah and say salam, so that these two become nafl for him, then he should follow the imam with the intention of fard. Explanation: This is the third case above. For example, Zuhr, 'Asr, or 'Isha, a four-rak'ah prayer, and he made sajdah on the first rak'ah, so he should add a second rak'ah and say salam, so that these two rak'ahs become nafl, and then join the imam with the intention of fard. Justification: So that both nafl is performed and participation in congregation occurs. Translation: (716) And if he has prayed three rak'ahs, he should complete it, then follow the imam with the intention of nafl in prayers other than 'Asr. Explanation: This is the fourth case. That it is a four-rak'ah prayer, e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha, and he has prayed three rak'ahs, so he should add the fourth rak'ah, this prayer will become fard, and then he should join the congregation as nafl. However, there is no nafl after 'Asr, so in 'Asr he should not join the congregation.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah deals with the chapter on catching the obligatory prayer (Bab Idrak al-Faridah). It is an expansion and commentary on the matn (core text), explaining the legal procedure for a person who has started praying individually and then finds a congregation. The passage presents four detailed scenarios and provides the fiqh reasoning behind each ruling. The author begins by stating the ruling (715): if one has made sajdah in a non-four-rak'ah prayer (like Fajr), he should break his prayer and join the congregation because he will complete his fard by joining a second rak'ah with the imam. However, if the prayer is Fajr and he has already completed both rak'ahs, he should not join because there is no nafl after Fajr. Then for a four-rak'ah prayer, three cases are distinguished: (1) if he has made sajdah in the first rak'ah, he should add a second rak'ah to make a pair (shaf'), then say salam, making it nafl, and then join the imam for fard. (2) if he has completed three rak'ahs, he should add the fourth to complete his fard and then join the congregation as nafl (except in 'Asr where nafl is prohibited after 'Asr). (3) if he has completed his fard already, he may join the congregation nafl based on the hadith of Jabir ibn Yazid al-Aswad. The hadith from Abu Dawud is quoted as proof that if one has already prayed his fard and then a congregation starts, he should pray with them and it will be considered nafl. The passage emphasizes that the hadith is the definitive proof for this concession. The commentary also clarifies the linguistic point that a rak'ah is only complete when sajdah is performed; before that, the rak'ah is not considered complete, so no harm is done by ending the prayer early. The translation and explanation (tashreeh) then elaborate on the application, highlighting that in 'Asr one cannot join as nafl after completing fard because of the prohibition of voluntary prayer after 'Asr. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi school's practical approach to balancing individual and congregational prayer, using both primary texts and rational reasoning (wajh).

Key Terms
رباعیۃ (ruba'iyyah): A prayer consisting of four rak'ahs, e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr, 'Isha.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; a single pair (two rak'ahs) is considered a complete unit of prayer in certain contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr (four-rak'ah fard) and made sajdah. He then finds the congregation for Zuhr. What should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) He should break his prayer immediately and join the congregation.
B) He should add a second rak'ah, say salam, making it nafl, then join the congregation for fard.
C) He should complete his prayer alone and then join the congregation for nafl.
D) He should not join the congregation because his prayer is already valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a structured concession to join the congregation even after starting salah alone, primarily by converting incomplete rak'ahs to nafl, except when nafl is prohibited (after 'Asr and after completing Fajr).

Ending Sunnah at Two Rak'ahs
Ruling on ending sunnah at two rak'ahs when khatib or iqamah calls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for ending the sunnah prayer of Jumu'ah or Zuhr at two rak'ahs when the khatib comes out or iqamah is called, and justify it using the shaf' principle.

Core Idea
When khatib or iqamah calls, end the sunnah at two rak'ahs — each pair is a complete unit (shaf').

We often think a prayer once started must be completed in full. But the Hanafi school teaches that certain sunnah prayers, especially the four-rak'ah sunnah of Jumu'ah and Zuhr, are structured as two independent pairs. This lesson explores the ruling that permits ending after the first two rak'ahs when an obligation—the khutbah or the congregation—takes precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the source to determine when this ruling applies: when praying the four-rak'ah sunnah of Jumu'ah or Zuhr, and the khatib emerges (for Jumu'ah) or iqamah is called (for Zuhr).
These are the two specific cases.
2
Understand the shaf' concept
Each two rak'ahs form a shaf' (pair), making the four-rak'ah sunnah two complete units. This is key to why stopping after two is permissible.
Shaf' is a recognized division in nafl prayers.
3
Apply the ruling
The ruling is to say salam after completing the first two rak'ahs (one shaf'), then join the congregation if possible, and later make up the remaining two rak'ahs.
The text says 'وهو الأوجه' — it is the most appropriate.
4
Justify the rationale
This avoids breaking the prayer abruptly and allows participation in the more important act (khutbah or congregational fard).
Balancing sunnah with wajib/obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۱۸) اور اگر جمعہ کی سنت پڑھتا ہو اور خطیب نکلے یا ظہر کی سنت میں اقامت کہی جاوے تو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے، پھر فرض کے بعد سنت کی قضا کر لے۔ اچھی بات یہی ہے۔ تشریح : جمعہ کی سنت چار رکعت ہے، اور ظہر کی سنت بھی چار رکعت ہے اور ان دونوں سنتوں کی ایک اہمیت ہے، البتہ ان میں ہر دورکعت ایک شفع ہے، اس لئے جمعہ کی سنت پڑھ رہا ہو اور خطیب خطبہ کے لئے نکل گیا تو اس وقت سنت پڑھنا اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک شفع یعنی دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے اور یہ سنت بعد میں پڑھے، یہی حال ظہر کی سنت کا ہے کہ سنت پڑھ رہا تھا اور فرض کی اقامت ہوگئی تو دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے اور جماعت کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے ۔ تا کہ نماز کو توڑنا بھی لازم نہ آئے اور جماعت میں بھی شرکت ہو جائے۔
Translation: (718) And if he is praying the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib comes out, or he is praying the sunnah of Zuhr and iqamah is called, then he should say salam at the end of two rak'ahs, then after the fard he should make up the sunnah. This is the best view. Explanation: The sunnah of Jumu'ah is four rak'ahs, and the sunnah of Zuhr is also four rak'ahs, and both these sunnahs have importance. However, every two rak'ahs in them form a shaf' (pair). Therefore, if he is praying the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib comes out for the khutbah, then continuing the sunnah at that time is not good, so he should complete one shaf' (two rak'ahs) and say salam, and pray the remaining after the fard. The same applies to the sunnah of Zuhr: if he is praying the sunnah and the iqamah for the fard is called, he should say salam after two rak'ahs and join the congregation, so that he does not have to break the prayer unnecessarily and also participates in the congregation.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling (718) for a situation where a person is engaged in the sunnah prayers of Jumu'ah or Zuhr (which are normally four rak'ahs, performed as two pairs of two) and then an impediment arises: for Jumu'ah, the khatib (the one delivering the khutbah) emerges, indicating the start of the Jumu'ah prayer; for Zuhr, the iqamah is called for the fard prayer. The ruling is to complete only two rak'ahs (one shaf') and then say salam, and afterwards, after the fard prayer, to make up the remaining two rak'ahs of the sunnah. The commentary explains the rationale: since each pair is a complete unit (shaf'), ending after the first pair does not break the prayer arbitrarily; it is a tidy stopping point. This avoids the necessity of breaking the prayer in the middle (which is disliked) and also allows one to attend the congregation or the khutbah. The phrase 'It is the best view' indicates that this is the preferred opinion within the Hanafi school. The ruling balances the virtue of completing the sunnah with the greater obligation of attending the congregational fard or listening to the khutbah.

Key Terms
خطیب (khatib): The person who delivers the Friday sermon (khutbah) before the Jumu'ah prayer.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs. In the context of sunnah prayers, two rak'ahs form one shaf' which is a complete unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is praying the four-rak'ah sunnah of Zuhr when iqamah is called. What should he do?
A) Complete all four rak'ahs and then join the congregation.
B) Say salam after the first two rak'ahs and then join the congregation, and pray the remaining two after the fard.
C) Break the prayer immediately by saying salam immediately without any condition.
D) Continue praying but make the intention to finish quickly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling permits ending a four-rak'ah sunnah at two rak'ahs when a more important obligation arises, due to the shaf' structure.

Joining the Imam in Fard Without Sunnah When Iqamah Is Called
Hadith-based ruling on priority of fard congregation over sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person entering the mosque when the imam is in fard, and explain the hadith proof that prohibits starting any sunnah prayer.

Core Idea
When iqamah is called, no prayer except the fard—join the congregation immediately.

You arrive at the mosque late. The iqamah has been called or the imam is already leading the fard prayer. Should you pray the sunnah of the time first? The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ), rules that you must join the congregation directly and not engage in any nafl or sunnah. This lesson unpacks the proof and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage describes a person entering the mosque when the imam is already in fard. The ruling is: he should follow the imam (iqtida) and not engage in sunnah.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites a hadith from Abu Hurairah (ra): 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the prescribed prayer (maktubah).' This is the primary dalil.
Hadith is from Sahih Muslim.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'fala salata illa al-maktubah' is a negation of any other prayer. In Hanafi usul, negation implies prohibition (tahrim). Thus, starting any nafl after iqamah is prohibited.
The negation is general and applies to all supererogatory prayers.
4
Determine the hukm level
Based on the strength of the dalil (zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala), the Hanafi school classifies this prohibition as makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
It is not haram because the hadith is ahad and the prohibition is not absolute.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
In practice, when you enter the mosque and find the jama'ah started, you must join immediately. Do not start any sunnah prayer even if you think you can finish quickly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: (۷۱۹) اور جو ایسے وقت میں آئے کہ امام فرض نماز میں ہو تو امام کے ساتھ اقتدا کرے اور سنت پڑھنے میں مشغول نہ ہو وجه : (۱) جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تو کوئی نماز نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله الله قال : (( اذا أقيمت الصلوة فلا صلوة الا المكتوبة ( مسلم شریف ، باب کراھیة الشروع في نافلة بعد شروع المؤذن في اقامة
Translation: (719) And whoever comes at a time when the imam is in the fard prayer, he should follow (iqtida) with the imam and should not engage in sunnah. Justification: (1) When the congregation has started, there is no other prayer. For this there is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (ﷺ) who said: 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the prescribed prayer (maktubah).' (Muslim, chapter on the dislike of starting a nafl after the beginning of the iqamah).
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage provides a fundamental ruling (719) and its proof: when a person arrives and finds the imam already leading the fard prayer, he must join the congregation immediately and should not occupy himself with any sunnah prayer (whether the regular sunnah of the time or any other nafl). The justification (wajh) quotes the famous hadith from Abu Hurairah (ra) reported in Sahih Muslim: 'When the iqamah is called, there is no prayer except the prescribed (maktubah).' This indicates that once the iqamah has been pronounced (or the imam has started the fard), it is forbidden to begin any other prayer. The Hanafi school applies this command as a strict prohibition (makruh tahrimi) of starting a nafl prayer when the congregation for fard is already in progress. The commentary highlights that the virtue of congregation overrides the desire to perform sunnah prayers. This ruling is essential for maintaining the communal aspect of prayer and ensuring that people do not miss the fard with the congregation by being preoccupied with optional prayers. The hadith is clear and strong, and the Hanafi school follows it as a definitive proof (dalil).

Key Terms
مکتوبہ (maktubah): The prescribed obligatory prayer (fard). In the hadith, it refers specifically to the fard for which the iqamah has been called.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he enters the mosque and finds the imam already in the fard prayer?
A) He should pray the sunnah of the time first, then join the congregation.
B) He should join the imam immediately without praying any sunnah.
C) He should wait for the next congregation.
D) He should pray in a corner and then leave.

Key Takeaway
When the iqamah is called, the only permissible prayer to begin is the prescribed fard; all supererogatory prayers are prohibited to start until after the congregation concludes.

Cutting Nafl Prayer When Iqamah Is Called During Third Rak'ah
Ruling on cutting supererogatory prayer to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for cutting a four-rak'ah nafl prayer when the iqamah is called during the third rak'ah, and identify the condition that triggers this ruling.

Core Idea
If you stand for the third rak'ah without sajdah, cut the nafl with salam; otherwise complete it.

The Hanafi school prioritizes joining the fard congregation over completing a nafl prayer. But the timing of cutting matters. In this lesson, we examine the precise moment when a four-rak'ah nafl can be safely terminated without sin or loss of reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the cutting of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer when the iqamah is called. The ruling is that it is recommended (sunnah) to cut with one salam while standing.
2
Locate the condition
The ruling applies only if one is standing in the third rak'ah and has not yet performed the sajdah of that rak'ah. This is the critical condition that makes cutting permissible.
If sajdah has been performed, the rak'ah is complete, and the person must finish all four rak'ahs.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person praying the four-rak'ah sunnah of Zuhr. He stands for the third rak'ah, recites the Fatiha and a surah, and is about to go into ruku when the iqamah is called. According to this ruling, he should say salam while standing and then join the fard congregation.
He must not complete the third rak'ah's sajdah.
4
Note the consequence of missing the condition
If he mistakenly performs sajdah before hearing the iqamah, or after hearing it but before cutting, he must then complete all four rak'ahs. He will then miss the beginning of the fard congregation.
The ruling emphasizes avoiding this scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۱۷) اور اگر تیسری رکعت میں کھڑے ہو جانے کے بعد سجدہ سے پہلے اقامت کہی جائے تو کھڑے کھڑے اصح روایت میں ایک سلام سے نماز قطع کر دے۔ تشریح : چار رکعت والی نماز تھی اور تیسری رکعت میں کھڑا ہوا اور ابھی سجدہ نہیں کیا اس لئے یہ رکعت پوری نہیں ہوئی اس لئے کھڑے کھڑے سلام پھیر دے اور جماعت کے ساتھ مل جائے۔ : اگر سجدے میں جائے گا تو چوتھی رکعت بھی پوری کرنی پڑے گی، اور فرض کی جماعت چھوٹ جائے گی ، اس لئے کھڑے کھڑے ہی سلام پھیر دے تا کہ چوتھی رکعت نہ پوری کرنی پڑے، اور آسانی سے جماعت میں مل جائے۔
Translation: (717) And if he is standing in the third rak'ah and the iqamah is said before his sajdah, then while standing, in the most correct narration, he should cut the prayer with one salam. Explanation: It was a four-rak'ah prayer, he stood for the third rak'ah, and has not yet done sajdah, so this rak'ah is not complete. Therefore, he should give salam while standing and join the congregation. Because if he goes into sajdah, he will have to complete the fourth rak'ah, and the fard congregation will be missed. So he gives salam while standing so as not to complete the fourth rak'ah, and he joins the congregation easily.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on how to handle a situation where a person is performing a four-rak'ah nafl prayer (like the sunnah of Zuhr, Asr, or Isha) and the iqamah for the fard congregation is called while he is in the third rak'ah, but before he has performed the sajdah of that rak'ah. The ruling, based on the preferred (asahh) narration, is that he should cut his nafl prayer by saying the salam while standing, without completing the third rak'ah or any additional rak'ahs. This is because the third rak'ah is not considered complete until the sajdah is performed, so he can terminate it easily. The reason is to avoid missing the fard congregation. However, if the third rak'ah's sajdah had been performed, he would have to complete the fourth rak'ah as the nafl would become fixed, and then he would miss the congregation. Also, note that this ruling does not apply to Asr prayer because no nafl is allowed after Asr.

Key Terms
اقتدى (iqtadā): To follow the imam in congregational prayer.
متنفلا (mutanaffilan): Performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
اصح (aṣaḥḥ): The most correct or preferred narration among the transmitted opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, if the iqamah is called while one is standing in the third rak'ah before sajdah, what should he do according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) Complete the third rak'ah and then say salam.
B) Say salam while standing without completing the rak'ah.
C) Continue the prayer and join the congregation later.
D) Sit down and wait until the iqamah ends.

Key Takeaway
When iqamah is called during the third rak'ah of a four-rak'ah nafl, cut the prayer with one salam while standing if you have not yet performed sajdah; otherwise complete all four.
